## 1. Connection config shapes per type (`app/datasources/*.py`)

**Snowflake** — `app/datasources/snowflake.py:57-91` (`SnowflakeConfig`):
```python
class SnowflakeConfig(BaseModel):
    model_config = ConfigDict(populate_by_name=True, extra="forbid")
    account: str
    user: str
    database: str
    schema_: str = Field(alias="schema")
    warehouse: str
    role: str | None = None
    auth_type: Literal["password", "key_pair"] = "password"
```
Account identifier: `config.account` (raw string, e.g. `"ab12345.eu-west-1"` per `tests/api/test_suites.py:43`). No normalization anywhere (see item 7). Default database/schema live on the **connection**, not the target: `config.database` / `config.schema_` (aliased from JSON key `"schema"`). DSN built at `snowflake.py:157`: `f"snowflake://{credentials}@{config.account}/{config.database}/{config.schema_}?{query}"`.

**Unity Catalog** — `app/datasources/unity_catalog.py:36-63` (`UnityCatalogConfig`):
```python
class UnityCatalogConfig(BaseModel):
    model_config = ConfigDict(extra="forbid")
    workspace_url: str
    warehouse_id: str
    @property
    def server_hostname(self) -&gt; str:
        return urlparse(self.workspace_url).netloc
```
Workspace host key = `workspace_url` (e.g. `https://adb-1234.5.azuredatabricks.net`); the actual hostname is a derived `.server_hostname` property.

**ADLS Gen2** — `app/datasources/adls.py:32-44` (`AdlsConfig`):
```python
class AdlsConfig(BaseModel):
    model_config = ConfigDict(extra="forbid")
    account_url: str
    container: str
    auth_type: Literal["sas", "managed_identity"] = "sas"
```
Account key = `account_url` (e.g. `https://&lt;account&gt;.blob.core.windows.net`); container key = `container`.

**S3** — `app/datasources/s3.py:32-46` (`S3Config`):
```python
class S3Config(BaseModel):
    model_config = ConfigDict(extra="forbid")
    bucket: str
    region: str
    auth_type: Literal["access_key", "iam_role"] = "access_key"
    access_key_id: str | None = None
```
Bucket key = `bucket`.

**Iceberg** — `app/datasources/iceberg.py:66-91` (`IcebergConfig`):
```python
class IcebergConfig(BaseModel):
    model_config = ConfigDict(extra="forbid")
    catalog_name: str = "default"
    catalog_type: IcebergCatalogType
    catalog_uri: str | None = None
    warehouse: str | None = None
    properties: dict[str, str] = {}
    secret_property: str | None = None
```
Catalog URI key = `catalog_uri` (required for `rest`/`sql`/`hive`, `iceberg.py:63` `_URI_REQUIRED`); warehouse/storage root key = `warehouse`.

## 2. `resolve_target()` — `app/services/run_target.py:82-137`

Full signature: `def resolve_target(conn_type: str, target: dict[str, Any] | None) -&gt; ResolvedTarget`.

`ResolvedTarget` (`run_target.py:69-79`):
```python
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class ResolvedTarget:
    table: str
    schema: str | None
    catalog: str | None
    batch: BatchSpec | None = None
```
Per-type resolution inside `resolve_target`:
- `adls_gen2`/`s3` (flat-file, `_FLATFILE_TYPES` at `run_target.py:45`): `table` = `path` (or unresolved if `pattern`/batch); `schema`/`catalog` = `None`.
- `snowflake` (`run_target.py:112-114`): `table = _require(target, "table", ...)`, `schema = _str_or_none(target.get("schema"))`, `catalog = None`.
- `unity_catalog` (`run_target.py:116-121`): `table` + required `catalog = _require(target, "catalog", ...)`, `schema` optional.
- `iceberg` (`run_target.py:123-132`): folds optional `namespace` into `table` as `f"{namespace}.{table}"`; `schema`/`catalog` stay `None`.
- Anything else (orchestration providers) → raises `SuiteTargetInvalidError` (422).

Companions: `validate_target(conn_type, target)` (`run_target.py:140-147`, write-time wrapper, just calls `resolve_target` and discards result) and `materialize_path(...)` (`run_target.py:150-186`, run-time-only, resolves flat-file `BatchSpec` to a concrete path via `flatfile.resolve_batch_file`).

**Callers** (`grep` results):
- `app/services/suite_service.py:101, 165` — `create_suite`/`update_suite` call `validate_target` at save time.
- `app/api/v1/suites.py:249` — manual run-trigger endpoint calls `resolve_target` before queuing a `Run`.
- `app/worker/tasks.py:119, 140, 442` — schedule dispatch (`resolve_target` + `materialize_path`).
- `app/mcp/server.py:305, 412, 419` — MCP tool `trigger_suite_run` + a profiling tool.
- `app/services/dryrun_service.py:103, 144` — dry-run path.
- `app/alerting/builder.py:31-54` (`_target_label`) — deliberately **doesn't** call `resolve_target` (must never raise while building a report); instead hand-rolls a dotted `catalog.namespace.schema.table` label — useful precedent for an asset-name formatter that also must not throw.

## 3. Suite save path — `app/services/suite_service.py`

- `create_suite` (`suite_service.py:69-113`): connection-exists / not-orchestration-provider checks, then `if target is not None: run_target.validate_target(connection.type, target)` at **line 101**, before constructing the `Suite` row (line 102). **This is the hook point for resolving/upserting an `Asset` on create.**
- `update_suite` (`suite_service.py:142-170`): same call at **line 165**, guarded by `if target is not None`. Also the hook point for re-resolving asset on target change. `connection_id` is immutable (doc comment lines 4-7), so asset resolution never needs to handle a connection swap mid-suite.
- No demo-suite seeding lives in `suite_service.py` itself — seeding is in `scripts/seed_dev.py` and `app/services/probe.py`/`ensure_probe_fixtures` (used by `app/api/v1/probe.py:66`, `tests/services/test_probe_seed.py`). These are the fixtures to check post-backfill for asset linkage.

## 4. Run dispatch path — all 4 `Run(...)` creation sites

```
app/api/v1/suites.py:251   run = Run(suite_id=suite.id, status="queued", triggered_by=f"manual:{current_user.id}")
app/api/v1/probe.py:68     run = Run(suite_id=suite.id, status="queued", triggered_by=f"probe:{current_user.id}")
app/mcp/server.py:306      run = Run(suite_id=suite.id, status="queued", triggered_by=f"mcp:{user.id}")
app/worker/tasks.py:452    run = Run(suite_id=suite.id, status="queued", triggered_by=f"schedule:{schedule.id}")
```
All four sites resolve/validate the target via `run_target.resolve_target` (or catch `DataQError` for schedules, `worker/tasks.py:441-450`) *before* constructing `Run(...)` — each `resolve_target` call site is the natural place to also stamp `run.asset_id` (the resolved target + connection are already in scope there). `Run` model: `app/db/models.py:376-397`; no `asset_id` column yet.

## 5. Migration precedents

Head revision: **`e716a1b2c3d4`** (confirmed via `alembic heads`).

Chain (most recent 3, in order):
1. `e716a1b2c3d4_widen_connection_type_for_iceberg.py` — widens `ck_connections_type_valid` to add `'iceberg'`; pure CHECK-constraint swap via `op.execute("ALTER TABLE ... DROP/ADD CONSTRAINT ...")`, no data rewrite.
2. `c605d1e2f3a4_add_runs_failure_reason.py` — adds nullable `runs.failure_reason` (`op.add_column`, no backfill).
3. `d2e3f4a5b6c7_per_suite_slack_email_notifications.py` — adds two nullable columns to `suite_notifications` (no backfill).

**Data-backfill precedent**: `alembic/versions/9c59b6a44f33_week3_schema_seam_check_kind_severity_.py` (rev `9c59b6a44f33`, down_revision `aa33d80c2158`). Two backfill techniques shown verbatim:

a) NOT NULL column backfilled via `server_default` (no explicit UPDATE needed):
```python
op.add_column(
    "checks",
    sa.Column("kind", sa.String(32), nullable=False, server_default="expectation"),
)
op.create_check_constraint(
    "kind_valid", "checks",
    "kind IN ('expectation', 'freshness', 'volume', 'schema_drift', 'anomaly', 'comparison')",
)
```

b) Explicit `op.execute` UPDATE backfill of existing rows to a new vocabulary **before** swapping the CHECK constraint (so the constraint never rejects in-flight data):
```python
op.execute("UPDATE results SET status = 'pass' WHERE status = 'passed'")
op.execute("UPDATE results SET status = 'fail' WHERE status IN ('failed', 'skipped')")
op.drop_constraint("status_valid", "results", type_="check")
op.create_check_constraint(
    "status_valid", "results",
    "status IN ('pass', 'warn', 'fail', 'critical')",
)
```
No migration in this repo uses `sa.table()` reflection-loop-style backfill (row-by-row Python loop) — all data rewrites are raw `op.execute(SQL)`. Follow this style for the assets backfill (e.g. `INSERT INTO assets (...) SELECT DISTINCT connection_id, target-&gt;&gt;'table', ... FROM suites WHERE target IS NOT NULL`).

ORM helper columns to reuse for the new `Asset` model (`app/db/models.py:85-108`):
```python
def _uuid_pk() -&gt; Mapped[uuid.UUID]:
    return mapped_column(UUID(as_uuid=True), primary_key=True, server_default=text("gen_random_uuid()"))
def _created_at() -&gt; Mapped[datetime]:
    return mapped_column(DateTime(timezone=True), nullable=False, server_default=func.now())
def _updated_at() -&gt; Mapped[datetime]:
    return mapped_column(DateTime(timezone=True), nullable=False, server_default=func.now(), onupdate=func.now())
def _in_check(column: str, values: tuple[str, ...], name: str) -&gt; CheckConstraint:
    ...
```

## 6. Test patterns

- Pure/unit style (no DB): `tests/services/test_run_target.py` — imports `resolve_target`/`validate_target`/`SuiteTargetInvalidError` directly, no fixtures. Example (verbatim, `test_run_target.py:24-26`):
```python
def test_snowflake_resolves_table_and_optional_schema() -&gt; None:
    r = resolve_target("snowflake", {"table": "ORDERS", "schema": "SALES"})
    assert (r.table, r.schema, r.catalog) == ("ORDERS", "SALES", None)
```
- DB-backed style (real Postgres via TestClient): `tests/api/test_suites.py` (docstring at top: "Suite endpoint tests against a real Postgres (`db_session`) via TestClient. `get_db` is overridden to the shared test session..."). Helper `_connection(db_session)` at `test_suites.py:37-51` inserts a `Connection` row directly for the target-suite FK — a good template for asset-resolution tests that need a real `Connection.config`.
- Pure-fake-session style (no DB, hand-rolled fakes): `tests/services/test_run_service.py` uses `FakeSession`/`FakeRunner` (not `db_session`) — see `test_successful_run_persists_results_and_marks_succeeded` at line 189.

Comparable service dirs: `tests/services/test_run_dispatch.py`, `tests/services/test_run_target.py`, `tests/api/test_suites.py`. No `test_suite_service.py` exists — suite-service behavior (including the `validate_target` hook) is exercised through `tests/api/test_suites.py`.

Adversarial harness — `tests/support/adversarial.py`: exposes `ADVERSARIAL_FRAMES: list[tuple[str, pd.DataFrame]]` (parametrize fixture of hostile single-column DataFrames — mixed types, NaN/Inf, unicode, bytes, Arrow-backed variants) and `assert_json_safe(value: Any) -&gt; None` (asserts `json.dumps(value, allow_nan=False)` succeeds). Two-line API: pass `ADVERSARIAL_FRAMES` into `pytest.mark.parametrize`, then call `assert_json_safe(...)` on any emitted value.

DB fixture: `tests/conftest.py` — `_db_engine` (session-scoped, `tests/conftest.py:169-198`, skips without `TEST_DATABASE_URL`/local Postgres, does `Base.metadata.create_all(engine)`) and `db_session` (`tests/conftest.py:201+`, function-scoped, uses `join_transaction_mode="create_savepoint"` so commits inside the test land on a savepoint that's rolled back after — tests never persist).

Created two new files for issue #757 (asset-identity resolver, ADR 0034), on the checked-out `feature/757-asset-entity` branch. Nothing was committed.

**`backend/app/services/asset_identity.py`** (214 lines) — `AssetIdentity` frozen dataclass + `resolve_asset_identity(conn_type, config, target)` + `normalize_snowflake_account(account)`, plus small pure per-datasource helpers (`_resolve_snowflake/_unity_catalog/_adls_gen2/_s3/_iceberg`, `_normalize_part`, `_pattern_base_prefix`, `_require_config/_require_target/_str_or_none`), styled after `run_target.py` (typed, `from __future__ import annotations`, `DataQError`-free — this one raises plain `ValueError` since it's a pure resolver with a fail-soft caller, per the spec).

I confirmed against the already-uncommitted `backend/app/services/asset_service.py` (the write-time caller from a different part of #757 already in this working tree) that its call `resolve_asset_identity(connection.type, connection.config, target)` matches my signature exactly — no adjustment needed.

**`backend/tests/services/test_asset_identity.py`** (345 lines, 44 tests) — covers every rule in the spec (Snowflake account normalization incl. whitespace/empty, quote-strip case folding, schema-override precedence; UC host/host:port, default schema, lower-fold, backtick quoting; ADLS blob/dfs URL account extraction + leading-slash strip; S3 bucket namespace + all three pattern base-prefix cases; Iceberg REST URI verbatim / `file` fallback / verbatim namespace folding; orchestration types + missing-key `ValueError`s; unicode round-trip and NUL-byte hostile inputs asserting a clean `ValueError`/non-crash rather than a stack trace).

**Verification (conda env `dataq`), all green:**
- `black` — no changes needed after 2 rewraps for line length
- `ruff check` — all checks passed
- `mypy backend/app/` — success, 99 source files (matches CI's `mypy backend/app/`)
- `mypy backend/tests/` — success, 107 source files (matches CI's `mypy backend/tests/`)

**Deviations from spec (both are test-design corrections, not implementation changes):**
1. My first draft of the "locator + region" Snowflake test used `"abc123.us-east-1"` — since `normalize_snowflake_account`'s literal rule checks for `-` *anywhere* in the string (per your spec, mirroring `fix_account_name`), a hyphenated region name collides with the org-account passthrough branch. Rewrote the test to use a hyphen-free fake region (`"abc123.uswest1"`) so it actually exercises the 2-segment `.aws`-append path. The implementation itself follows your literal spec unchanged.
2. For the "plain path, no glob" pattern case, I initially expected the full literal pattern back; on reflection (and per docs/post-v1-assets-lineage-incidents-notes.md §1 — "a flat-file pattern's asset is its literal base directory/prefix"), the algorithm consistently base-prefixes to the containing directory even when no glob metacharacter is present, so I corrected the test's expected value to `"retail/orders/"` rather than changing the implementation.

No other files were modified (the pre-existing uncommitted `Asset` model in `backend/app/db/models.py` and `asset_service.py` from other in-flight #757 work were left untouched, as instructed — I only read them to confirm the calling contract matches).</result>

## Summary

Implemented the schema + wiring half of #757 (asset entity, ADR 0034) on branch `feature/757-asset-entity`, coding against the sibling's `asset_identity.resolve_asset_identity`.

### Files created
- **`backend/alembic/versions/f8b9c0d1e2a3_add_assets_entity.py`** — migration (revision `f8b9c0d1e2a3`, down_revision `e716a1b2c3d4`). Creates `assets` (+ unique `(namespace, name)`), adds nullable `suites.asset_id` / `runs.asset_id` FKs (ON DELETE SET NULL) + indexes, and a self-contained Python backfill that is a **deliberately frozen copy** of the resolver logic (byte-identical to `asset_identity.py` as of this revision; documented as such). Backfill dedups on identity, pulls env/connection_id from the suite's connection, and skips unresolvable suites fail-soft. Runs are not backfilled (history stays NULL, by design).
- **`backend/app/services/asset_service.py`** — `resolve_and_upsert_asset(session, connection, target)`; upserts via `pg_insert(...).on_conflict_do_update(index_elements=["namespace","name"], set_=last_seen/env/connection_id).returning(id)`. Never raises (two fail-soft guards + structlog warnings).
- **`backend/tests/services/test_asset_service.py`** — 8 tests (100% coverage of the module).

### Files changed
- **`backend/app/db/models.py`** — `Asset` model (+ `Text` import, `__all__`), `asset_id` + index on `Suite` and `Run`, docstrings in the file's voice.
- **`backend/app/services/suite_service.py`** — `create_suite` and `update_suite` (target-not-None branch) set `asset_id` via the fail-soft hook.
- **4 Run sites stamped** `asset_id=suite.asset_id`: `api/v1/suites.py`, `api/v1/probe.py`, `mcp/server.py`, `worker/tasks.py`.
- **`backend/app/services/orchestration_service.py`** — 5th run site (the `pg_insert(Run)` pipeline-success trigger) stamped via a `Suite.asset_id` scalar subquery (scope addition — see deviations).
- **`backend/tests/api/test_suites.py`** (+3 tests: create links asset, update re-points, unresolvable-config → asset NULL fail-soft) and **`test_runs.py`** (+1: trigger stamps run.asset_id).

### Verification
- **Migration up/down/up**: verified on a throwaway DB. Seeded suites → backfill produced one deduped asset `snowflake://ab12345.eu-west-1` / `RETAIL.SALES.ORDERS`, targetless + bad-target suites left NULL; `downgrade -1` cleanly dropped table + both columns; re-upgrade re-ran green. Throwaway DB dropped.
- **Tests**: 286 passed across all touched areas (asset_service 8, asset_identity sibling, suites, runs, probe, orchestration, worker, mcp). asset_service.py at 100% coverage.
- **Gates**: `black --check` clean (235 files), `ruff check` clean, `mypy backend/app/` (99 files) + `mypy backend/tests/` (108 files) clean, `bandit -c pyproject.toml -r backend/app` 0 issues.

### Spec deviations (with reasons)
1. **Added a 5th run-stamp site** (orchestration-triggered runs in `_trigger_suites`) beyond the 4 constructor sites listed. The design says "runs stamp asset_id at dispatch"; leaving orchestration-triggered runs NULL would be an inconsistency. Done inline via scalar subquery (single INSERT, no extra round-trip).
2. **`last_seen`-bump test backdates the row first.** Postgres `now()` is transaction-start time, fixed within the single-transaction test harness, so a naive second-`now()` comparison can't observe the bump. Runtime behavior is unchanged (`SET last_seen = now()` per the spec).
3. **Migration backfill logs skips at INFO** rather than a bare `continue` (satisfies ruff S112 + gives operators visibility). Still fail-soft.
4. **Note (not a deviation):** `ab12345.eu-west-1` normalizes to itself (no `.aws` suffix) because it contains a hyphen (`eu-west-1`) → the OL passthrough branch fires first. This matches the sibling's rule exactly and is reflected in the tests.

No commits/pushes made. The sibling's `asset_identity.py` / `test_asset_identity.py` were left untouched.</result>

<result>[{"file":"backend/app/services/asset_service.py","line":56,"summary":"resolve_and_upsert_asset's second try/except (around the pg_insert upsert at lines 56-83) catches any exception from session.execute(stmt) and returns None, but never calls session.rollback() or uses a SAVEPOINT (session.begin_nested()). The docstring/comment claims this 'must NEVER fail a suite save', re-establishing the old invariant that suite creation could never be blocked by an unrelated side effect — but if the upsert statement actually fails against a real Postgres connection (constraint violation, transient DB error, statement timeout), the SQLAlchemy Session's transaction is left in a failed/aborted state. <note>A task-notification fires each time this agent stops with no live background children of its own. The user can send it another message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than once.</note>
<result>## 1. Exact function body

```python
def fix_account_name(name: str) -&gt; str:
    """
    Normalize Snowflake account name according to OpenLineage specification.

    Snowflake supports two formats:
    1. Organization-account format (preferred): orgname-accountname
       - Never includes region or cloud in the identifier
       - Example: myorg-myaccount

    2. Account locator format (legacy): accountlocator[.region[.cloud]]
       - Examples:
         - xy12345 → xy12345.us-west-1.aws (AWS US West Oregon default)
         - xy12345.us-east-1 → xy12345.us-east-1.aws (aws default)
         - xy12345.us-east-2.aws → xy12345.us-east-2.aws
         - xy12345.east-us-2.azure → xy12345.east-us-2.azure
    """
    # Split by dots to analyze the structure
    parts = name.split(".")

    # First part is the account identifier
    account_part = parts[0]

    # Check if it's organization-account format (contains hyphen)
    # Organization-account format never has region/cloud info
    if "-" in account_part:
        # Organization-account format - return as-is
        return account_part

    # Account locator format - need to include region and cloud
    if len(parts) == 1:
        # Just account locator, add default region and cloud (AWS US West Oregon)
        return f"{account_part}.us-west-1.aws"
    elif len(parts) == 2:
        # account_locator.region, add default cloud (aws)
        return f"{account_part}.{parts[1]}.aws"
    else:
        # Full format: account_locator.region.cloud
        return name
```

## 2. Input → output

- `myorg-myaccount` → `myorg-myaccount`
- `xy12345` → `xy12345.us-west-1.aws`
- `xy12345.us-east-1` → `xy12345.us-east-1.aws`
- `xy12345.us-east-2.aws` → `xy12345.us-east-2.aws` (unchanged)
- `xy12345.eu-west-1` → `xy12345.eu-west-1.aws`

## 3. Hyphen scoping

The hyphen check tests only `account_part` (`parts[0]`, the segment before the first dot) — not the string as a whole.

**Verdict: scoped to the first segment only** — a hyphen inside a later segment (e.g. `us-east-1` in `xy12345.us-east-1`) does NOT trigger org-account passthrough, so `.aws` IS still appended, giving `xy12345.us-east-1.aws`.

## 4. Case-folding

None — no `.lower()`/`.upper()`/case-folding anywhere in `fix_account_name`.</result>

<result>I have comprehensive context now. Here is the full report.

## Issue #758 scope (verbatim)

```
title: feat(lineage): OpenLineage emission from run_service — RunEvents +
       DataQualityAssertions/metrics facets, dark by default

- `openlineage-python` (Apache-2.0, license-checked) emit hooks in `run_service`:
  START on dispatch, COMPLETE/FAIL on finish; job namespace `dataq`, job name from
  the suite; the target asset as input `Dataset`.
- `DataQualityAssertionsDatasetFacet` per check result (check → `assertion`,
  outcome → `success`, severity tier → `severity`, observed/expected →
  `actual`/`expected`); `DataQualityMetricsInputDatasetFacet` for `metric_value`
  monitor kinds (freshness/volume — ADR 0012).
- Dark by default: no transport configured → no emission; `OPENLINEAGE_DISABLED`
  honored; standard `OPENLINEAGE__TRANSPORT__*` env config; failures to emit
  never fail the run (fail-open, logged).
- One emitter reaches Marquez/DataHub(native OL HTTP receiver)/Kafka with zero
  per-catalog code.

Acceptance criteria:
- [ ] START/COMPLETE/FAIL events with correct dataset naming (matches #757
      resolver output byte-for-byte)
- [ ] Assertions + metrics facets populated from real result rows; PII
      discipline: no sample rows in events
- [ ] Off-by-default verified (no config → zero network calls); emit failure
      cannot fail or slow a run (fail-open test)
- [ ] Verified end-to-end against a local Marquez (compose) receiving events
```
Design precedent, `docs/post-v1-assets-lineage-incidents-notes.md` lines 58-64: "Console transport by default, `OPENLINEAGE_DISABLED` honored — dark by default, zero new required infra". ADR 0034 decision 3a (`docs/adr/0034-asset-entity-openlineage-identity-lineage-pull.md:18`): "Dark by default (console transport, `OPENLINEAGE_DISABLED` honored)". **Note the tension**: the design notes say "console transport by default" (which is openlineage-python's own library default when no transport is configured — it writes JSON to stdout, not the network) but the acceptance criteria demand "no config → zero network calls" AND the user's framing says "no config → no client, zero emission." Since console transport is *not* zero-emission (it does emit, just to stdout, and constructs a client), the implementation must **not** rely on the library's own default — it must gate client construction explicitly (mirroring the `otel.py` pattern below), only building an `OpenLineageClient` when an explicit DataQ-level toggle/transport is configured, exactly like the OTel exporters.

---

## 1. Run lifecycle — hook points

`/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/services/run_service.py`

There are **two** entry points that drive a run to `running`, and **three** places a run reaches terminal:

- `execute_run` (line 172-251) — the normal path. START hook: `run.status = "running"` at line 189, committed at line 191 (before the try block). Terminal hooks:
  - success: lines 217-227 (`run.status = "succeeded"`, `finished_at`, `failure_reason = None`, `session.commit()`)
  - cooperative-cancel-during-execution: lines 217-220 and 230-234 (returns early, run stays `cancelled` — **not** a COMPLETE/FAIL case per the issue's own scope, which only lists START/COMPLETE/FAIL)
  - failure: lines 228-243 (`except Exception`, `run.status = "failed"`, `failure_reason = classify_failure_reason(exc)`, `session.commit()`, then `return run` at line 243)
- `skip_run` (line 254-276) — the "no data to check" path. START hook: line 264-266 (`run.status = "running"`, commit). Terminal (always succeeds): lines 272-274 (`run.status = "succeeded"`, `finished_at`, commit).

There is **no single terminal choke point inside `run_service`** — `execute_run`'s success/failure branches and `skip_run`'s success are three separate commit sites. The closest thing to a single choke point is one level up, in the worker:

`/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/worker/tasks.py`
```python
@celery_app.task(name="run_suite")
def run_suite(run_id: str) -&gt; str:
    rid = uuid.UUID(run_id)
    session = get_session()
    try:
        outcome = _run_suite(session, run_id=rid)
        alert_dispatch.publish_run_outcome(session, run_id=rid)   # &lt;-- lines 193-194
        return outcome
    finally:
        session.close()
```
`alert_dispatch.publish_run_outcome` (below) is exactly this kind of terminal choke point already, and is the closest existing precedent for "one place, after the run reaches a terminal state, fire a best-effort side-effect." But it only fires after `_run_suite` returns — i.e. after **all** of `_run_suite`'s paths (setup-failed, materialize-failed, skip, or `execute_run`) have already committed their terminal status. It does **not** cover the START event (that has to be hooked inside `execute_run`/`skip_run` directly, or by wrapping `run.status = "running"` assignment sites).

`_run_suite` (tasks.py lines 85-176) also has two more terminal-failed sites before `execute_run` is even reached — `_terminal_failed` (lines 66-82, used at line 129 for setup failure and line 152 for materialize failure). These never call `execute_run`, so if OL START must correspond 1:1 with an actual run attempt, these early failures need their own consideration (arguably no START was ever emitted for them, so no FAIL either, or a START+FAIL pair right there — spec decision needed).

Suite/checks access in `_run_suite`: `suite = session.get(Suite, run.suite_id)` (tasks.py:115), `checks = list(session.scalars(select(Check).where(Check.suite_id == suite.id)))` (tasks.py:120). Post-#757, `run.asset_id` is already stamped at construction time by `run_dispatch.new_queued_run`:
```python
# app/services/run_dispatch.py:41-46
return Run(
    suite_id=suite.id,
    asset_id=suite.asset_id,
    status="queued",
    triggered_by=triggered_by,
)
```
So inside `execute_run`/`skip_run`, `run.asset_id` is available directly off the `Run` object passed in — no extra query needed for the id itself, but the **Asset row** (namespace/name) is a separate table and does need a fetch (see §3).

---

## 2. Results shape at completion — what's in memory, no re-query needed

`_build_result` (`run_service.py:57-95`) builds one `Result` per check from a `CheckOutcome`, all in the `rows` list built at `run_service.py:209-212`:
```python
rows = [
    _build_result(run.id, check, check_outcome)
    for check, check_outcome in zip(checks, outcomes, strict=True)
]
session.add_all(rows)
```
This `rows: list[Result]` (unpersisted-but-populated ORM objects) is exactly what's in memory at the moment the run completes — the emitter can build its facets straight from this list plus the parallel `checks: list[Check]` (already in scope), with **zero extra DB query**. Result fields (`app/db/models.py:485-513`): `status` (str, one of `RESULT_STATUSES`), `metric_value` (Decimal|None), `observed_value`/`expected_value`/`sample_failures` (JSONB dict|None). `Check` fields (`models.py:347-380`): `name`, `kind` (`expectation`/`freshness`/`volume`/...), `expectation_type`, `warn_threshold`/`fail_threshold`/`critical_threshold`, `config` (JSONB).

Severity vocabulary (`app/db/models.py:37-71`):
```python
RUN_STATUSES = ("queued", "running", "succeeded", "failed", "cancelled")
_RESULT_SEVERITY_TIERS = ("pass", "warn", "fail", "critical")
_RESULT_OPERATIONAL_STATUSES = ("skip", "error")
RESULT_STATUSES = _RESULT_SEVERITY_TIERS + _RESULT_OPERATIONAL_STATUSES
SEVERITY_RANK: dict[str, int] = {
    tier: rank for rank, tier in enumerate((t for t in _RESULT_SEVERITY_TIERS if t != "pass"), 1)
}
FAILING_TIERS: tuple[str, ...] = tuple(SEVERITY_RANK)   # ("warn","fail","critical")

def worst_severity(statuses: Iterable[str]) -&gt; str | None:
    present = [s for s in statuses if s in FAILING_TIERS]
    return max(present, key=lambda s: SEVERITY_RANK[s]) if present else None
```
`worst_severity` is already imported into `run_service.py` (line 43) and used at `run_service.py:345` for the runs-list rollup — the emitter's per-run/run-level `severity` (if a single run-level severity is wanted) should reuse this exact helper rather than reimplementing an ordering.

`resolve_status`/`extract_metric` (`app/services/severity.py:33-123`) is the single place that derives `(status, metric_value)` — already called at `run_service.py:73-78` inside `_build_result`. The metrics facet (`metric_value` monitor kinds — freshness/volume) reads `Result.metric_value` directly; `check.kind in MONITOR_KINDS` (`app/datasources/monitors.py:33-35`: `FRESHNESS = "freshness"`, `VOLUME = "volume"`, `MONITOR_KINDS = (FRESHNESS, VOLUME)`) is the discriminator for which checks get the metrics facet vs. the plain assertions facet.

`skip_run` (`run_service.py:267-270`) builds a different, simpler shape — every check gets `status="skip"`, `observed_value={"reason": reason}` — the emitter needs to handle this case too (no assertion outcome really applies; `skip` isn't in `FAILING_TIERS` so `worst_severity` naturally ignores it).

---

## 3. Asset access

`Asset` model (`app/db/models.py:153-195`, added by #757):
```python
class Asset(Base):
    __tablename__ = "assets"
    __table_args__ = (UniqueConstraint("namespace", "name", name="uq_assets_namespace_name"),)

    id: Mapped[uuid.UUID] = _uuid_pk()
    namespace: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(Text, nullable=False)
    name: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(Text, nullable=False)
    env: Mapped[str | None] = mapped_column(String(16))
    connection_id: Mapped[uuid.UUID | None] = mapped_column(
        UUID(as_uuid=True), ForeignKey("connections.id", ondelete="SET NULL")
    )
    owner_user_id: Mapped[uuid.UUID | None] = mapped_column(
        UUID(as_uuid=True), ForeignKey("users.id", ondelete="SET NULL")
    )
    first_seen: Mapped[datetime] = mapped_column(DateTime(timezone=True), nullable=False, server_default=func.now())
    last_seen: Mapped[datetime] = mapped_column(DateTime(timezone=True), nullable=False, server_default=func.now())
```
`namespace`+`name` is exactly the OL Dataset identity (see `Asset` docstring, `models.py:162-173`, and `asset_identity.py`'s `resolve_asset_identity`/`AssetIdentity(namespace, name)`).

Loading it in the worker session: `Run.asset_id` is a nullable FK to `assets.id` (SET NULL on delete, `models.py:467-469`). In `_run_suite` (tasks.py), nothing currently loads the `Asset` row — only `run.asset_id` (a bare UUID) exists on the `Run`. The emitter needs `session.get(Asset, run.asset_id)` (same idiom as `session.get(Suite, run.suite_id)` at tasks.py:115 / `session.get(Run, run_id)` at tasks.py:102) guarded for `None` (targetless suite / unresolved asset → `run.asset_id is None` → no input Dataset, or skip emission of that facet — fail-soft per the `Asset` FK comment "SET NULL so an asset sweep never deletes a run", `models.py:466`).

Note `FakeSession` in the test suite (`tests/services/test_run_service.py:20-49`) has **no `.get()` method** — only `add_all`/`commit`/`rollback`/`refresh`. If the emitter hook lives inside `execute_run`/`skip_run` and needs to fetch the `Asset` row itself, either (a) `FakeSession` gains a `.get`, or (b) — cleaner — the caller (`_run_suite` in tasks.py, which already has a real session) resolves the `Asset` once and passes it into `execute_run`/`skip_run`/the emitter as a parameter, keeping `run_service`'s pure/fake-testable contract intact. This is a design decision the spec needs to make explicit.

---

## 4. Dependency conventions

`/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/requirements.txt` — pin style is **exact `==`** throughout, one dependency per line, grouped by concern with a `# ── Section ──` comment header, and an inline `#` comment explaining *why* pinned when non-obvious (CVE/compat reasons). File header (lines 1-14) declares it as the **single source of truth**; `requirements-dev.txt` and `requirements-typecheck.txt` must mirror versions.

Examples:
```
fastapi==0.138.2
uvicorn[standard]==0.50.2
python-multipart==0.0.32          # required for FastAPI form data; CVE-2026-24486/40347/42561 (was 0.0.20)
...
opentelemetry-sdk==1.43.0                        # spans (A3) + logs (#524) — vendor-neutral core, ADR 0010
opentelemetry-exporter-otlp-proto-http==1.43.0   # generic OTLP/HTTP backend for spans + logs (#589) — any OTLP consumer (Tempo/Jaeger/Datadog), vendor-neutral (ADR 0010)
```
An `openlineage-python` line would go in a new `# ── Lineage emission ──` (or similar) section, exact-pinned, with a comment noting Apache-2.0 + ADR 0034/#758.

Test-only deps: `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/requirements-dev.txt`:
```
-r requirements.txt
-r requirements-typecheck.txt
-r requirements-tooling.txt

# ── Testing ──
pytest==9.1.1                     # CVE-2025-71176 (was 8.4.2)
pytest-asyncio==1.4.0
pytest-cov==7.1.0
httpx==0.28.1                     # async test client for FastAPI
```
(`requirements-typecheck.txt` is the *typed subset* mypy needs — only add `openlineage-python` there too if/when it ships type stubs and is imported unconditionally somewhere mypy walks; given the lazy-import pattern below, it likely should **not** need to go there since mypy only sees it under `TYPE_CHECKING`.)

**Lazy-import pattern** (repo convention, from `app/core/secrets.py` header comment: "The Azure SDK and the redis client are **lazy-imported** so deployments that don't use them don't pay the import cost.") — concrete instances:

```python
# app/core/secrets.py:105-115 (AzureKeyVaultStore._client_lazy)
def _client_lazy(self) -&gt; SecretClient:
    if self._client is not None:
        return self._client
    with self._lock:
        if self._client is None:
            from azure.identity import DefaultAzureCredential
            from azure.keyvault.secrets import SecretClient

            self._client = SecretClient(
                vault_url=self._vault_url,
                credential=DefaultAzureCredential(),
            )
        return self._client
```
and the module-level `TYPE_CHECKING`-only import at the top (`secrets.py:31-32`):
```python
if TYPE_CHECKING:
    from azure.keyvault.secrets import SecretClient
```
Same pattern in `app/core/otel.py:52-56, 76-78`:
```python
def build_span_exporters(settings: Settings | None = None) -&gt; list[SpanExporter]:
    settings = settings or get_settings()
    exporters: list[SpanExporter] = []
    conn = settings.applicationinsights_connection_string
    if conn:
        from azure.monitor.opentelemetry.exporter import AzureMonitorTraceExporter
        exporters.append(AzureMonitorTraceExporter(connection_string=conn))
    base = _otlp_base(settings)
    if base:
        from opentelemetry.exporter.otlp.proto.http.trace_exporter import OTLPSpanExporter
        exporters.append(OTLPSpanExporter(endpoint=f"{base}/v1/traces"))
    return exporters
```
This is the exact shape the OL emitter should copy: `TYPE_CHECKING`-only top-level import for the type (`OpenLineageClient`), a lazy `from openlineage.client import OpenLineageClient` **inside** the gated branch, so an unconfigured deployment (dark by default) never imports the package at all.

---

## 5. Settings conventions &amp; the OTel dark-by-default gating precedent

`/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/core/config.py:8-19`:
```python
class Settings(BaseSettings):
    model_config = SettingsConfigDict(
        env_file=".env.app",
        env_file_encoding="utf-8",
        extra="forbid",
        case_sensitive=False,
    )
```
`extra="forbid"` is documented (comment, lines 10-14) as catching **typo'd/stale keys in `.env.app`** — it does not reject arbitrary process-environment variables that don't correspond to a declared field. I verified this empirically:
```
$ OPENLINEAGE__TRANSPORT__TYPE=http TOTALLY_UNRELATED_ENV_VAR_XYZ=1 python3 -c \
    "from backend.app.core.config import Settings; print(Settings(_env_file=None).environment)"
dev   # no error
```
So a standard, non-`DATAQ`-prefixed env var like `OPENLINEAGE__TRANSPORT__TYPE` or `OPENLINEAGE_DISABLED` will **not** trip `extra=forbid` as long as it isn't also written into `.env.app` under a name that happens to collide with (but not match the type of) a Settings field. It simply won't be read by `Settings` at all — which is fine, because `openlineage-python`'s own `OpenLineageClient()`/`OpenLineageConfig` reads those vars itself; DataQ's `Settings` only needs its own DataQ-prefixed toggle for the "is emission configured at all" gate (e.g. an `openlineage_transport_url: str | None = None` or reuse of `OPENLINEAGE_URL`/`OPENLINEAGE_DISABLED` presence-checked via `os.environ` directly, mirroring how `secrets.py`'s `EnvSecretStore` reads `KV_SECRET_*` straight from `os.environ` rather than through `Settings`).

**The OTel exporter seam is the closest precedent for the dark-by-default gate itself** (`app/core/otel.py` docstring, lines 1-23, and `build_span_exporters`/`build_log_exporters`, lines 51-79):
```python
"""...
Two exporters sit behind the seam and **may both be active at once**:
- **Azure Monitor** — when ``APPLICATIONINSIGHTS_CONNECTION_STRING`` is set.
- **Generic OTLP/HTTP** — when ``OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT`` is set (#589) ...

Neither set ⇒ telemetry is a complete no-op (the pre-#524 ``AzureLogHandler`` gate).

All exporter imports are **lazy** (repo convention, see ``secrets.py``) so a
deployment that uses neither backend never pays the import cost.
"""
...
def build_span_exporters(settings: Settings | None = None) -&gt; list[SpanExporter]:
    settings = settings or get_settings()
    exporters: list[SpanExporter] = []
    conn = settings.applicationinsights_connection_string
    if conn:
        from azure.monitor.opentelemetry.exporter import AzureMonitorTraceExporter
        exporters.append(AzureMonitorTraceExporter(connection_string=conn))
    base = _otlp_base(settings)
    if base:
        from opentelemetry.exporter.otlp.proto.http.trace_exporter import OTLPSpanExporter
        exporters.append(OTLPSpanExporter(endpoint=f"{base}/v1/traces"))
    return exporters
```
And the empty-list-means-off short-circuit in the caller (`app/core/logging.py:105-108`):
```python
settings = get_settings()
exporters = otel.build_log_exporters(settings=settings)
if not exporters:
    return
```
This "config value present → lazily import + construct → append to a list; caller returns/no-ops on empty list" is the pattern the OL emitter should mirror: `_build_openlineage_client(settings) -&gt; OpenLineageClient | None`, returning `None` when unconfigured, with the emit call sites doing `if client is None: return` before touching anything OL-related.

---

## 6. PII discipline — what must never leave the app

The redaction seam lives in two places that must both stay untouched by the emitter's design: (1) `core/logging.py`'s structlog `_redact_pii` processor (`app/core/logging.py:14-46, 66-77`), which redacts **log lines** by key-name (`password`, `token`, `email`, etc.) and by regex over string values (secret query-params, URL userinfo credentials) — this governs anything the emitter logs on a fail-open catch, not the OL payload itself. (2) `run_service.redact_sample_failures` (`app/services/run_service.py:587-656`) and its docstring (lines 594-615), which governs what may cross the **read API** boundary for `Result.sample_failures` specifically.

Critically, **`sample_failures` is the only Result column that can carry real row data** — the `Result` model comment says it plainly (`app/db/models.py` — see also `run_service.py:679-681`: "`sample_failures` is the only result column that can carry real (possibly PII-bearing) data rows"). By contrast, `observed_value`/`expected_value` are documented and, by inspection of `_build_result` (`run_service.py:57-95`) and the GX runner's shape, **aggregate scalars/summaries, not row values**: `observed_value = sanitize_json(outcome.observed_value)` is populated from GX's observed-value dict (e.g. `{"observed_value": 5}` — a count/percentage), and for an errored check it's just `{"error": &lt;message&gt;}` — explicitly called out as safe because "GX exception messages are schema-level (no row data)" (`run_service.py:69-71`). `expected_value` mirrors the check's config (e.g. `{"column": "id"}`) — schema metadata, not data. So the facet-building code should read `observed_value`/`expected_value`/`metric_value`/`status`/check `name`/`column`/`expectation_type` freely, but **must never read `sample_failures`** — that field alone carries potential PII/row values and is exactly what the OL `DataQualityAssertionsDatasetFacet`/metrics facet must stay clear of, matching the acceptance criterion "no sample rows in events."

One paragraph for the spec: nothing that reaches an OpenLineage RunEvent may include `Result.sample_failures` (partial_unexpected_list / unexpected_index_list — real row values, the only PII-bearing result column) or any raw exception text (`run.failure_reason` is already a fixed, classified, redaction-safe string via `classify_failure_reason`, `app/services/failure_classifier.py` — safe to include; a raw caught exception's `str(exc)` is not, mirroring the "never surface raw adapter text" rule already enforced in `execute_run`'s except-block, `run_service.py:235-240`). Everything else the facets need — check name, column (from `check.config.get("column")`), expectation_type, status, metric_value, observed/expected aggregate JSON — is schema/aggregate-only and safe by the same reasoning `run_service.py`'s own docstrings already establish for those fields.

---

## 7. Test patterns for the worker/services layer

`run_service` is tested with **no DB, no GX**: a `FakeSession` (`tests/services/test_run_service.py:20-49`) records `add_all`'d rows and counts `commit`/`rollback`, plus a `refresh` stub that can simulate a concurrent status change; a `FakeRunner`/`FakeMonitorRunner` (lines 62-147ish) returns canned `SuiteOutcome`/`CheckOutcome` or raises. Tests call `run_service.execute_run(_sess(session), run=run, checks=checks, runner=runner, table=..., schema=...)` directly (e.g. `test_successful_run_persists_results_and_marks_succeeded`, lines 189-224; `test_runner_exception_marks_failed_and_persists_no_results`, lines 267-282) and assert on `run.status`, `session.added`, `session.commits`/`rollbacks`. **This is the harness an OL-emit hook inside `execute_run`/`skip_run` would be tested through** — a fake/spy "emitter" (or a monkeypatched `emit` function) injected the same way `FakeRunner` is, asserting it was called with the right `RunEvent` shape and that a raised exception from it doesn't propagate out of `execute_run`.

The **"no network by default" / fail-open assertion pattern** already exists for the alerting publishers, and is the direct template to reuse:

```python
# tests/alerting/test_slack_email_publishers.py:181-184
def test_slack_noop_when_unconfigured(db_session: Any) -&gt; None:
    """No webhook secret name → never touches the network."""
    pub = SlackPublisher(secret_store=_Store({}), webhook_secret_name=None, allowed_hosts=())
    pub.publish(db_session, _report(worst="fail"))  # must not raise / post
```
and, for asserting zero network calls via a monkeypatched sink:
```python
# tests/alerting/test_slack_email_publishers.py:462-468
def test_slack_publish_noop_when_webhook_secret_missing(
    db_session: Any, monkeypatch: pytest.MonkeyPatch
) -&gt; None:
    posted: list[object] = []
    monkeypatch.setattr("backend.app.alerting.slack.httpx.post", lambda *a, **k: posted.append(a))
    _slack_publisher(_Store({})).publish(db_session, _report(worst="fail"))
    assert posted == []
```
For the OL emitter, the equivalent would monkeypatch the lazily-imported `OpenLineageClient`/its `.emit` (or the module-level client factory) and assert it's never constructed/called when no transport env is set — plus a **fail-open** test modeled on `run_service.py`'s own `test_runner_exception_marks_failed_and_persists_no_results` (lines 267-282): inject an emitter whose call raises, and assert `execute_run`'s return value / `run.status` / `session.commits` are completely unaffected (mirroring `alert_dispatch.publish_run_outcome`'s own `except Exception: log.exception(...); return False` at `app/alerting/dispatch.py:59-61`, which is the canonical "best-effort, never raises, run already persisted" wrapper to copy for the OL emit call sites).

## 8. Celery worker lifecycle — client construction

There is **no per-worker-boot heavyweight-client-init hook currently in use** for this class of dependency — the repo's existing precedent (secret store, OTel exporters, result publisher) is a **process-wide lazy singleton built on first use and cached**, not a Celery signal-based init:

- `app/alerting/registry.py:29-77` — `get_result_publisher()` builds a `CompositePublisher` once (`_publisher_singleton`, guarded by `_publisher_lock`), with `reset_result_publisher_cache()` for tests.
- `app/core/secrets.py` — `AzureKeyVaultStore`/`RedisSecretStore` lazily build their client on first `.get`/`.set` call (`_client_lazy`, guarded by a per-instance `threading.Lock`), not at import or worker-boot time; `get_secret_store()` (referenced throughout `tasks.py`, e.g. line 125) is itself presumably an `lru_cache`d factory (same shape as `config.get_settings`, `app/core/config.py:203-205`, `@lru_cache(maxsize=1)`).

Celery **does** use signals for other cross-cutting concerns — `celery_app.py:16-23` imports `beat_init`, `before_task_publish`, `setup_logging`, `task_postrun`, `task_prerun`, `worker_process_init` from `celery.signals` (used elsewhere, e.g. `configure_logging`/`configure_tracing`/`instrument_celery` at worker boot, and the request-id correlation on `before_task_publish`/`task_prerun`/`task_postrun`) — so `worker_process_init` is an available, already-imported hook if the OL client needs one-time-per-worker-process setup (e.g. registering an `os.register_at_fork` handler the way the OTel `BatchLogRecordProcessor` does per `logging.py:114-118`'s comment on fork-safety). But **the norm for a config-gated, possibly-absent client in this codebase is a lazily-built, `lru_cache`/module-level-singleton-with-lock, not a Celery signal** — the spec should follow `get_secret_store`/`get_result_publisher`'s shape (a `get_openlineage_client() -&gt; OpenLineageClient | None` cached singleton) rather than introducing a new signal-based init path.</result>

## Summary

Implemented dark-by-default OpenLineage emission for suite runs (ADR 0034 decision 3a, gap G-d phase-1). Working tree only — nothing committed.

### Files created
- `backend/app/lineage/__init__.py` — package doc
- `backend/app/lineage/emitter.py` — env gate + cached client singleton + pure `RunEvent` builders
- `backend/app/lineage/dispatch.py` — fail-open choke point (`emit_run_lineage_start` / `emit_run_lineage_terminal`)
- `backend/tests/lineage/__init__.py`, `conftest.py`, `test_emitter.py`, `test_dispatch.py`

### Files changed
- `backend/app/worker/tasks.py` — import `lineage_dispatch`; bracket `_run_suite` with START (before) + terminal (after), next to `alert_dispatch.publish_run_outcome`
- `backend/requirements.txt` — new Lineage section, `openlineage-python==1.51.0`
- `pyproject.toml` — added `openlineage.*` to the mypy `follow_imports="skip"` override (keeps slim-CI and local typechecking identical; no addition to `requirements-typecheck.txt` needed)
- `backend/tests/worker/test_tasks.py` — task-level test asserting the START→terminal hook order

### Per-AC status
- START/COMPLETE/FAIL/ABORT with correct dataset naming — DONE. runId=`str(run.id)`, job namespace `dataq` / name=suite.name, producer `https://github.com/TheurgicDuke771/DataQ`, input `Dataset(namespace, name)` read straight off the `assets` row (#757 identity, so byte-for-byte).
- Assertions + metrics facets from real rows; no sample rows — DONE. One assertion per (check,result); skip omitted; error→success=False; severity warn→"warn", fail/critical→"error". Volume `rowCount` from `metric_value`. FAIL adds `ErrorMessageRunFacet(message=run.failure_reason, programmingLanguage="python", no stackTrace)`. Dedicated PII test serializes a full terminal event and asserts a `sample_failures` sentinel never appears.
- Off-by-default; emit failure can't fail/slow a run — DONE. `is_emission_configured()` reads env directly; `_ExplodingSession` test proves zero queries on the dark path (client None returns before any session access); a `boom` client proves emit exceptions are swallowed.
- End-to-end vs local Marquez (compose) — NOT done here (requires the #762 Marquez compose stack, which is a separate issue). Serde round-trip against the real openlineage 1.51.0 classes is verified in tests instead.

### Test result
Full suite: **1700 passed, 1 skipped, 98.32%** coverage (gate ≥80 met). New package: `dispatch.py` 100%, `emitter.py` 99% (only the lock double-check `return` on the concurrency path is uncovered). Black/Ruff/mypy(app+tests)/Bandit all clean. `pip-audit -r backend/requirements-dev.txt`: **No known vulnerabilities found**.

### Dependency
`openlineage-python==1.51.0` — license **Apache-2.0** (rule-40 compliant). Core transitive deps only (no kafka/gcp/msk extras pulled): `attrs`, `python-dateutil`, `pyyaml`, `requests`, `httpx`, `packaging` — all permissively licensed, pip-audit-clean. Installed into the `dataq` conda env.

### Deviations (with reasons)
1. **Hook in `worker/tasks.py`, not `run_service`** — the pre-agreed documented deviation. The task layer is the single choke point covering execute/skip/early-fail with a guaranteed 1:1 START+terminal pair per runId, and leaves run_service's FakeSession contract untouched. Sits beside the existing `alert_dispatch` precedent.
2. **`observed_value`/`expected_value` deliberately excluded from the assertion facet** (the issue text suggested mapping them to `actual`/`expected`). The `Assertion` class does support those fields, but some GX expectations put *actual failing column values* in `observed_value`, so including it risks PII leakage. Per the locked design's "when in doubt, exclude" and the hard PII rule, I dropped them. Only the outcome + severity + column name leave the process.
3. **Volume `rowCount = int(metric_value)`** — implemented exactly as the locked design specifies. Flagging one semantic caveat for your awareness: an ADR-0012 volume monitor's `metric_value` is the *deviation %*, not the row count (the true count lives in `observed_value["row_count"]`). I followed the locked instruction rather than deviate, but if the intent was the literal row count, this should point at `observed_value["row_count"]` instead — your call.
4. **Builders use lazy openlineage imports inside functions** (not top-level in the module), matching the otel.py/secrets.py convention, so the dark path pays no import cost. Because the package is py.typed and absent from the slim CI typecheck env, I routed it through the existing `follow_imports="skip"` mypy block rather than adding it to `requirements-typecheck.txt` — no `typecheck-deps-sync` impact.

Severity is supported by the installed `Assertion` class (confirmed via signature inspection), so it is populated.</result>

<result>Analyzing the PR #765 diff against the four efficiency angles:

1. **env reads on dark path**: The dark path (unconfigured) checks `_client_configured` boolean first (line 196, emitter.py) and returns immediately with no lock, no env read. Env is only read ONCE on first ever call behind lock. **Not flagged** — no wasted work on dark path.

2. **duplicate query loading Checks+Results**: Yes, terminal dispatch (dispatch.py lines 93-94) queries checks and results again after `_run_suite` loaded checks at tasks.py line 121. However, the angle explicitly says "flag only with a cheaper alternative that doesn't break the choke-point design." The choke-point isolates lineage emission; passing data through would couple modules. **Not flagged** — design trade-off is acceptable.

3. **sync HTTP emit latency**: Lines 68 and 95 emit synchronously. OpenLineage-python client does support async transports in theory, but: (a) no async infrastructure is already in place, (b) fire-and-forget breaks fail-open contract, (c) at single-tenant scale, emit latency (100s ms) is trivial vs datasource runtime (10s+ sec). **Not flagged** — latency is trivially cheap.

4. **client reconstruction per call**: Client is lock-guarded singleton (lines 169-171, 195-216), constructed once and cached. Both emit calls use cached instance. **Not flagged** — no reconstruction.

**Additional scan**: Asset loaded twice (lines 67, 92), but primary-key lookups hit session identity map on second call (same session object passed to both). Checks/results query unavoidable (results created during execution, must be queried). Both queries are indexed and trivially cheap at single-tenant scale.

<result># Issue #759 Research — Files &amp; Excerpts for the Implementation Spec

## Issue text (verbatim, `gh issue view 759`)

**Body:**
&gt; G-d build slice (design: `docs/post-v1-assets-lineage-incidents-notes.md` §2.2, ADR 0034 decision 3b; filed by #596). Depends on #757. Extends the ADR-0029 dbt provider — the 3-scheme artifact reader (`file`/`adls`/`s3`) fetches the sibling `manifest.json` already landing at `&lt;artifacts_uri&gt;/latest/` unconsumed.
&gt; - Parse the **minimal stable subset only**... Table-level edges: models/seeds/snapshots + sources only... ephemeral models collapsed...
&gt; - Map nodes → assets via the #757 resolver; upsert into `lineage_edges(upstream_asset_id, downstream_asset_id, source, last_seen)`... Refresh on the existing 10-min poll beat.
&gt; - Blast-radius query...
&gt; - Test bed: the harness dbt project (4 `RETAIL` sources → 4 `ANALYTICS_STG` views → 2 `ANALYTICS` marts)...

**Comment (2026-07-10, the refresh-propagation AC referenced in your request):**
&gt; **Explicit refresh-propagation scenario (user-requested AC, 2026-07-10):** after lineage is first built, *change* the lineage at the source — edit a dbt model's `ref()`/`source()` set (add an edge, remove an edge, add a model) and rebuild so a new `manifest.json` lands — and verify DataQ converges: new edges appear after the next poll (or webhook-triggered refresh — the dbt success event should trigger an immediate manifest re-read rather than waiting up to 10 min for the beat), removed edges age out via `last_seen` and stop appearing in blast-radius output. Test as a two-fixture sequence (manifest v1 → manifest v2) asserting the edge diff, plus the staleness cutoff.

#757 (dependency, CLOSED) shipped the `assets` table + `resolve_asset_identity` resolver — details below.

## 1. The dbt artifact reader — `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/orchestration/dbt.py`

**`_read_artifact` signature** (dbt.py:102):
```python
def _read_artifact(config: DbtConfig, job: str, secret: str) -&gt; bytes | None:
```
No filename/relpath parameter — the relpath is a **module-level constant**, hardcoded to `run_results.json` (dbt.py:37):
```python
_RUN_RESULTS_RELPATH = "latest/run_results.json"
```
Each scheme branch composes `&lt;artifacts_uri&gt;/&lt;job&gt;/&lt;_RUN_RESULTS_RELPATH&gt;` directly:
- `file`: dbt.py:113-117 — `Path(parsed.path) / job / _RUN_RESULTS_RELPATH`, `None` if `path.exists()` is false.
- `adls`: dbt.py:119-146 — `blob = f"{prefix}/{job}/{_RUN_RESULTS_RELPATH}"`; `BlobServiceClient` with 10s connect/read timeouts; `ResourceNotFoundError` → `None`.
- `s3`: dbt.py:148-173 — `key = f"{prefix}/{job}/{_RUN_RESULTS_RELPATH}"`; `boto3.client("s3", ...)`; `ClientError` with `NoSuchKey`/`404` → `None`; other `ClientError`s (and any transport/auth error) re-raise.

**Answer: not reusable as-is.** `_RUN_RESULTS_RELPATH` is baked into every branch's path/blob-key/S3-key string; there's no parameter to swap in `latest/manifest.json`. The straightforward refactor is to add a `relpath: str` (or `filename: str`) parameter to `_read_artifact`, defaulting to `_RUN_RESULTS_RELPATH` for existing call sites, and add a sibling constant e.g. `_MANIFEST_RELPATH = "latest/manifest.json"` for the new caller. (`config: DbtConfig` and `secret` stay unchanged — same store, same credential, same 10s timeout policy.)

**`DbtConfig` model** (dbt.py:56-99), the dbt connection's non-secret config:
```python
class DbtConfig(BaseModel):
    model_config = ConfigDict(extra="forbid")
    project_name: str
    artifacts_uri: str
    jobs: list[str]
    region: str | None = None
    access_key_id: str | None = None
```
- `artifacts_uri` — base location (`adls://…`, `s3://…`, `file:///…`), scheme-validated (dbt.py:80-86), trailing slash stripped.
- `jobs` — non-empty list of job names, each read at `&lt;artifacts_uri&gt;/&lt;job&gt;/latest/…`.
- `region`/`access_key_id` — S3-only, non-secret halves of the credential (`_s3_needs_access_key` model_validator, dbt.py:95-99).
- **No `account`, `database`, `warehouse`, or any Snowflake-identity field** — confirmed by `extra="forbid"` (any surprise key raises, tested at `tests/orchestration/test_dbt_provider.py:151-153`, `test_config_forbids_extra`).

The class docstring (dbt.py:56-69) is explicit that the *only* per-connection secret is the artifacts-store read credential — there is no warehouse credential/identity here at all.

---

## 2. The poll flow + the post-success seam

**Poll entry point / beat task** — `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/worker/tasks.py`:
- `_poll_orchestration_runs(...)` (tasks.py:290-363) — iterates every `Connection` of type in `ORCHESTRATION_PROVIDERS`, calls `provider_impl.list_recent_runs(...)` then `orchestration_service.ingest_polled_runs(...)`.
- `poll_orchestration_runs` celery task (tasks.py:391-398), registered name `"poll_orchestration_runs"`.
- Beat schedule — `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/worker/celery_app.py` (~line 62-66):
```python
beat_schedule={
    "poll-orchestration-runs": {
        "task": "poll_orchestration_runs",
        "schedule": 600.0,  # 10 minutes
    },
    ...
```
Per-connection provider instances are built via `get_orchestration_provider(connection.type)` (tasks.py:336, registry.py:29-32) — a stateless singleton dict lookup (`registry.py:20-24`), not per-connection construction; `dict(connection.config)` + the secret are passed as plain args into `list_recent_runs`.

**The exact provider-agnostic success seam — `_trigger_suites`** in `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/services/orchestration_service.py`:
```python
def _trigger_suites(
    session: Session, *, provider: str, connection: Connection, update: RunUpdate
) -&gt; list[Run]:
```
(orchestration_service.py:197-273) — called from **both** flows, gated identically on `update.status == "succeeded"`:
- Webhook flow, `ingest_event` (orchestration_service.py:308-343), lines 338-341:
```python
triggered = (
    _trigger_suites(session, provider=provider, connection=connection, update=update)
    if update.status == "succeeded"
    else []
)
```
- Poll flow, `ingest_polled_runs` (orchestration_service.py:353-401), lines 397-400:
```python
if update.status == "succeeded":
    triggered.extend(
        _trigger_suites(session, provider=provider, connection=connection, update=update)
    )
```
Both call sites take a plain `provider: str` + `connection: Connection` + the already-normalized `RunUpdate` — no provider branching visible here; `_trigger_suites` itself only queries `TriggerBinding` by `(provider, pipeline_or_dag_id, env)`, still provider-agnostic.

**Does `OrchestrationProvider` have any optional capability hook already?** No. `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/orchestration/base.py:77-116` — the `Protocol` only declares `provider`, `resource_config_key`, `parse_event`, `fetch_run_detail`, `list_recent_runs`. I grepped for `hasattr(provider_impl` / `getattr(provider_impl` across `orchestration/*.py`, `orchestration_service.py`, `worker/tasks.py` — zero hits. The only "optional" pattern in this seam is `fetch_run_detail` raising `NotImplementedError` to mean "no enrichment" (caught in `_maybe_enrich`, orchestration_service.py:176-179) — i.e. optionality-via-exception, not optionality-via-hasattr.

**Implication for #759:** the analogous hook point is the two identical `if update.status == "succeeded": _trigger_suites(...)` blocks (orchestration_service.py:338-341 and 397-400). Per CLAUDE.md §11 ("Don't bypass the `OrchestrationProvider` abstraction with provider-specific branching in service code" — CLAUDE.md:235), a `refresh_lineage`-type side effect must NOT be `if provider == "dbt": ...` in `orchestration_service.py`. Since no optional-capability convention exists yet, the spec needs to introduce one — e.g. an optional `OrchestrationProvider.on_success(config, secret, connection) -&gt; None` method (default no-op, or checked via `getattr(provider_impl, "refresh_lineage", None)` the way `fetch_run_detail`'s `NotImplementedError` is checked), called from both `ingest_event` and `ingest_polled_runs` alongside `_trigger_suites`, right where `update.status == "succeeded"` is already tested — no new provider-name conditional needed since only `DbtProvider` would implement the hook.

## 3. Snowflake identity mapping — what the dbt connection config actually stores

Confirmed from `DbtConfig` above (dbt.py:56-78): **no account/database/warehouse field, `extra="forbid"` rejects any add-hoc key.** `DbtConnectionAdapter.validate_config`/`test` (dbt.py:196-208) just delegates to `DbtConfig.model_validate` — nothing extra stashed.

**The #757 resolver** — `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/services/asset_identity.py`:
```python
def resolve_asset_identity(
    conn_type: str, config: dict[str, Any], target: dict[str, Any]
) -&gt; AssetIdentity:
    ...
    if conn_type == "snowflake":
        return _resolve_snowflake(config, target)
    ...
    raise ValueError(f"connection type {conn_type!r} has no asset identity (not a datasource)")
```
(asset_identity.py:57-76) and `_resolve_snowflake` (asset_identity.py:104-113):
```python
def _resolve_snowflake(config: dict[str, Any], target: dict[str, Any]) -&gt; AssetIdentity:
    account = _require(config, "account", "snowflake", "config")
    database = _require(config, "database", "snowflake", "config")
    ...
    namespace = f"snowflake://{normalize_snowflake_account(account)}"
    name = ".".join(_normalize_part(part, engine="snowflake") for part in (database, schema, table))
    return AssetIdentity(namespace=namespace, name=name)
```
The docstring is explicit (asset_identity.py:30-33): **orchestration connection types (adf/airflow/dbt) have no asset identity and raise `ValueError`** — this resolver categorically cannot be called with the dbt connection's config to get a namespace; it needs a Snowflake connection's `config["account"]`/`config["database"]`, which the dbt connection doesn't carry and which the harness manifest/profiles.yml route (per your prompt) isn't available either.

**What #757 already produced:** the `assets` table (migration `f8b9c0d1e2a3_add_assets_entity.py`) backfilled every existing suite's target through this exact resolver, keyed `(namespace, name)` unique (models.py:176). For the harness project's Snowflake suites (RETAIL/ANALYTICS_STG/ANALYTICS tables — confirmed pattern `RETAIL.SALES.ORDERS`-style names at `tests/services/test_asset_identity.py:61,71,80`), those rows already carry `namespace = snowflake://{normalized harness account}` from the **real Snowflake connection's own config**, resolved at suite-save time — a route the dbt manifest parser has no access to.

**Conclusion (option (b) is the only viable route in-repo today):** since the dbt connection config carries neither account nor database/warehouse identity, and profiles.yml isn't fetched, the manifest→asset mapping cannot construct a `namespace` from anything the dbt connection or manifest offers by itself. The manifest node's `database.schema.alias` (case-folded per the Snowflake `_normalize_part`/`normalize_snowflake_account` rules already in `asset_identity.py`) is only the **`name`** half of an OL asset key — matching must join on that `name` string against existing `assets` rows (populated by #757 from real Snowflake suite targets) and take the row's own `namespace`. Nodes whose `name` has no existing asset match (e.g. a mart nobody has a suite on yet) have no reliable namespace to fabricate and should be left unmapped/skipped rather than inventing a `namespace`, consistent with #757's fail-soft posture (`f8b9c0d1e2a3_add_assets_entity.py:201-206`, "fail-soft: bad/legacy target → leave asset_id NULL").

## 5. `models.py` tail — Asset model + naming conventions

`/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/backend/app/db/models.py` — 704 lines total. The `Asset` model (models.py:153-195):
```python
class Asset(Base):
    __tablename__ = "assets"
    __table_args__ = (UniqueConstraint("namespace", "name", name="uq_assets_namespace_name"),)

    id: Mapped[uuid.UUID] = _uuid_pk()
    namespace: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(Text, nullable=False)
    name: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(Text, nullable=False)
    env: Mapped[str | None] = mapped_column(String(16))
    connection_id: Mapped[uuid.UUID | None] = mapped_column(
        UUID(as_uuid=True), ForeignKey("connections.id", ondelete="SET NULL")
    )
    owner_user_id: Mapped[uuid.UUID | None] = mapped_column(
        UUID(as_uuid=True), ForeignKey("users.id", ondelete="SET NULL")
    )
    first_seen: Mapped[datetime] = mapped_column(
        DateTime(timezone=True), nullable=False, server_default=func.now()
    )
    last_seen: Mapped[datetime] = mapped_column(
        DateTime(timezone=True), nullable=False, server_default=func.now()
    )
```
File ends with `SuiteNotification` (models.py ~575-651) then `__all__` (models.py ~656-704), currently: `Asset, Base, Check, Connection, PipelineRun, Result, Run, Schedule, Share, Suite, SuiteNotification, TriggerBinding, User` — **no `LineageEdge` yet**; a new model would append after `SuiteNotification`, before `__all__`, and be added to that list.

**Conventions to mirror for `lineage_edges`** (from `Asset` + `TriggerBinding`/`PipelineRun`, models.py throughout):
- `__tablename__` snake_case plural.
- `UniqueConstraint(..., name="uq_&lt;table&gt;_&lt;cols&gt;")`, `Index("ix_&lt;table&gt;_&lt;col&gt;", ...)`, `ForeignKeyConstraint`/FK naming `fk_&lt;table&gt;_&lt;col&gt;` (matches the migration's `op.create_foreign_key("fk_suites_asset_id", ...)`, `op.create_index("ix_suites_asset_id", ...)`).
- `id: Mapped[uuid.UUID] = _uuid_pk()` helper for the PK.
- `first_seen`/`last_seen` pattern (both `DateTime(timezone=True)`, `nullable=False`, `server_default=func.now()`) — directly reusable for `lineage_edges.last_seen` (upstream/downstream would need `upstream_asset_id`/`downstream_asset_id` FKs to `assets.id`, likely `ondelete="CASCADE"` since an edge is meaningless once either endpoint asset is gone — unlike `Asset.connection_id`'s `SET NULL`, which preserves an asset past its source connection).
- `source` column (per issue body `lineage_edges(upstream_asset_id, downstream_asset_id, source, last_seen)`) would want a `String`/`Text` + likely a `_in_check(...)`-style CHECK constraint (pattern used elsewhere, e.g. `Connection.__table_args__` at models.py:200-201) if `source` is an enum (e.g. `'dbt'`).
- A natural unique constraint would be `(upstream_asset_id, downstream_asset_id, source)` to make the poll's re-parse an upsert (mirrors `uq_assets_namespace_name`, `uq_pipeline_runs_provider_run`).

New-module coverage: `dbt_manifest.py` 97%, `edges.py` 93%.

### Deviations (2, both reported per instruction)
1. **Timestamp clock for the prune**: used `clock_timestamp()` (wall clock, advances within a transaction) for edge `last_seen` and `refresh_started_at`, instead of `now()`/`transaction_timestamp()`. **Reason**: the test harness's `db_session` uses `join_transaction_mode="create_savepoint"`, so both refreshes in the AC test share one outer transaction where `now()` is constant — the prune's strict `&lt;` would never fire. `clock_timestamp()` makes pruning correct regardless of transaction boundaries (strictly more robust; production separate-transactions would also work with `now()`). Documented inline.
2. **Fixture v2 formatting**: generated deterministically from v1 with only the three intended graph edits, but reserialized (`indent=2, sort_keys=True`) so whitespace/key-order differs from v1 rather than being byte-identical. Semantic content is otherwise unchanged; the parser and tests are formatting-independent. The generator was an inline script, no scratch file left.</result>

<result>## Live UC Schema-Drift Detection Test — Final Report

### Critical incident (flag first)

**A live Databricks PAT was inadvertently printed to command output during this session.** While verifying schema cleanup, I ran `conda run -n dataq python -c "..." "$PAT"` — passing the PAT as a positional CLI argument instead of via `os.environ` (violating the "env/command-substitution only, never argv" rule). The script raised a syntax error, and `conda run`'s failure handler echoed its **full invoked command line, including the PAT value in plaintext**, into my visible output. This is a genuine credential exposure of `dataq-app-kv-aw6laj/conn-unity-catalog-retail` (the live UC PAT). **Recommend rotating this PAT immediately** and treating it as compromised. All other credential handling in this session followed the inline-fetch-only pattern correctly; this was a single isolated mistake, caught and not repeated (the retry used `os.environ` only).

### Per-scenario verdict

| Scenario | Verdict | Evidence |
|---|---|---|
| **Drift 1 — column added** (`discount_pct`) | **DETECTED** | `expect_table_columns_to_match_set` → `status: fail`, `observed_value: {"observed_value": ["amount","discount_pct","id","status"]}` vs `expected_value: {"column_set": ["id","status","amount"]}`. | **Drift 2 — column removed** (`status`) | **DETECTED (partially, as an error not a clean fail)** | Column-set check fails (observed 3-col set missing `status`). The not-null check on the now-missing `status` column comes back `status: "error"` with `observed_value: {"error": "Error: The column \"status\" in BatchData does not exist."}` — a raw GX/pandas exception string surfaced verbatim to the API consumer, not a DataQ-authored user-facing message. |
| **Drift 3 — type changed** (`id BIGINT→STRING`) | **DETECTED** | `expect_column_values_to_be_of_type` → `fail`, `observed_value: {"observed_value": "str"}` vs `expected_value: {"type_": "int64", "column": "id"}`. Note: GX's pandas backend reports the *Python value type name* (`"str"`), not the pandas dtype (`"object"`) — a calibration gotcha for anyone authoring this check type against UC. |

### DataQ bugs / UX gaps found

**1. (Bug, high severity) `check_id`↔result content misattribution when any check errors.** In both drift2 and drift3 runs, `GET /runs/{run_id}` returned `results[]` where each entry's `check_id` pointed to the *wrong* check's config/observed/expected values, in a consistent rotation. Root cause (confirmed by reading GX 1.17.2 source + DataQ code, not speculative):
- GX's `Validator.graph_validate` builds its results list in **two passes** — errored expectations are appended first (`validator.py:781-798`), then all remaining pass/fail expectations in original order (`validator.py:642-667`). So once any expectation errors, GX's `gx_result.results` order no longer matches submission order.
- `backend/app/datasources/gx_runner.py:123` (`to_suite_outcome`) copies GX's list order verbatim with no re-sort.
- `backend/app/services/run_service.py:138` and `:211` zip `SuiteOutcome.checks` positionally back onto the original `checks` list/ids (`zip(checks, outcomes, strict=True)`), assuming order is preserved.
- Net effect: a UI/API consumer reading a run with a missing-column error will see check results **attributed to the wrong check** — e.g. the not-null check's "column does not exist" error shown against the column-set check's id, and vice versa. This is silent, high-confidence-looking corruption of result data, not merely a display glitch. **File a GitHub issue for this** — this is a real, previously-unknown defect surfaced only because this test triggered a genuine metric-computation error (missing column), which the baseline and drift1 (clean fail, no error) runs didn't exercise.

**2. (Minor/by-design, but confusing) `checks_total` excludes errored checks.** `checks_total=2` while `results` has 3 entries in drift2/drift3 is intentional (`run_service.py` `check_outcome_counts` only tallies pass/warn/fail/critical tiers, deliberately excluding `skip`/`error`), but combined with bug #1 it makes the run summary actively misleading — worth reconsidering whether `checks_total` should reflect all executed checks regardless of tier.

**3. (UX gap) Raw exception string surfaced as `observed_value.error`.** `"Error: The column \"status\" in BatchData does not exist."` is a raw pandas/GX exception message passed straight through to API consumers with no DataQ-level normalization (e.g. no structured `missing_column` reason code). Fine for an engineer, poor for an end-user-facing alert/dashboard.

**4. (Positive finding)** The `expect_column_values_to_be_of_type` "int64" guess for a UC `BIGINT` column worked correctly on the first try (no recalibration run needed) — useful precedent for future UC check authoring.

- No leftover local DataQ objects remain related to this test.

The run-stamped ORDER_LINES asset (`0776a30e`) and the dbt-refresh node resolved to the **same row** — no duplicate. ## (f) Bugs / gaps found

**No DataQ bugs.** The parser, anchor/pin, identity unification, connection-scoped prune, and fail-open dispatch all behaved to spec. Observations:
1. **Orphaned asset row is by design:** `DATAQ_DB.ANALYTICS.RPT_ORDER_REVENUE_DAILY` (`16ba4e46`) remains in `assets` after the drop, with `last_seen` frozen at the add-refresh (00:47:57) — subsequent refreshes correctly don't touch it. Matches ADR 0034: "asset rows accrete… `last_seen` + a sweep, not deletes, is the cleanup posture." The frozen `last_seen` is the right sweep signal.
2. **Config-mapping footgun (docs-only):** the harness publishes to `raw/dbt/latest/`, so the DataQ connection must be `artifacts_uri=adls://…/raw` + `jobs=["dbt"]` — the harness's own `DBT_ARTIFACTS_URI` (`adls://…/raw/dbt`) does not slot in verbatim as `artifacts_uri`. Worth a line in the dbt-connection docs.
3. **Harness-side gap (not DataQ):** `AZURE_STORAGE_CONNECTION_STRING` is not in `secrets.sh` (only TF-injected into the ACA job), so the documented local `run.sh` upload path silently no-ops/fails locally; I minted it inline from `az storage account show-connection-string`. Also, my earlier `test -n \"$VAR\"` probe was a false positive (escaped quotes) — the var was never set.
4. `triggered: 0` on every poll — correct (no `trigger_bindings` for the dbt job).

## Summary

**Branch:** `fix/issue-767-result-attribution` (commit `d709f9f9`, not pushed)

### Mechanism chosen: positional meta-marker (the preferred approach)
I verified empirically against the installed GX 1.17.2 (conda env `dataq`) that (a) the error-first reorder is real — submitting `[id, nope(errors), amt]` returns `[nope, id, amt]` — and (b) `meta={"dataq_index": i}` **propagates verbatim** onto each result's `expectation_config.meta` and stays out of `.kwargs` (so it never leaks into `expected_value`). Both facts confirmed, so the meta-marker path (not multiset matching) is used. It is duplicate-safe: two checks with identical `expectation_type`+`kwargs` get distinct indices and stay 1:1.

### Files changed
- **`backend/app/datasources/gx_runner.py`** — the whole fix lives in the shared GX translation layer, so every runner (snowflake/flatfile/unity_catalog/iceberg — all route through `run_expectations` → `_execute`) is covered centrally:
  - `_to_gx_expectation(spec, index=None)` gains an optional `index`; when set it stamps `meta={"dataq_index": i}` (merged with any caller meta). Default-None preserves the existing re-exported/test callers.
  - `_execute` builds the suite with `_to_gx_expectation(check, index=i)` per check.
  - New `_submission_index` / `_in_submission_order` helpers; `to_suite_outcome` now iterates results **re-sorted by the marker**, falling back to GX's list order if any result lacks a marker (keeps constructed unit-test results working). `run_service` is untouched — its positional-zip order contract is now actually guaranteed instead of assumed.
- **`backend/tests/datasources/test_flatfile.py`** — 2 real-GX end-to-end regression tests (pandas path, real missing-column error): the errored check submitted **last** so the reorder actively breaks positional mapping; plus a duplicate-identical-expectations test.
- **`backend/tests/datasources/test_gx_runner.py`** — 3 unit tests on `to_suite_outcome`: explicit error-first reorder simulation, all-pass order preserved, and no-marker fallback.

### Red/green proof
- **Red:** stashing only the source fix (tests intact), the 3 new attribution tests **failed** against pre-fix code — e.g. `test_run_checks_errored_check_maps_to_its_own_spec_despite_gx_reorder` and `test_to_suite_outcome_reorders_errored_first_gx_result`, with the errored "column does not exist" content landing on the wrong outcome position (the exact live cross-wiring).
- **Green:** with the fix restored, all 5 new tests pass; the full `backend/tests/datasources/` + `backend/tests/services/` run is **715 passed, 135 skipped** (skips are the deferred live-datasource network seams).

Neither is an attribution bug; file separately if desired.
