<result>All checks green. The work is complete on branch `feature/issue-761-incidents` (7 commits, clean tree, not pushed).

## Summary — Issue #761: incident objects (G-d phase 3)

**Branch:** `feature/issue-761-incidents` (off `main` @ `a4093c04`). Not pushed, no PR.

**Migration:** `c4e5a6b7d8f9` (add_incidents), chained off `f0a1b2c3d4e5`. Single head verified before AND after (`alembic heads` → `c4e5a6b7d8f9 (head)`); up→down→up green through the real alembic graph on a scratch DB (table + partial unique index + `auto_resolve_incidents` default all confirmed). Additive only.

**State machine (5 lines):**
1. A breaching result (warn/fail/critical) opens a new incident for `(asset_id, check_id)` via `INSERT … ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` on the partial unique index (`active = open|acknowledged`).
2. On conflict it falls through to attach: `occurrence_count++`, `last_seen_at` + evidence refreshed — never a duplicate (upsert-race-safe, #420).
3. The first passing result auto-resolves the active incident (`resolved_by=auto`), default-on per-suite `auto_resolve_incidents` toggle; `skip`/`error` are no-ops.
4. Manual `ack` (open→acknowledged) and `resolve` (→resolved, `resolved_by=user`) always win; a resolved row is never re-mutated (409 on double-resolve / ack-of-resolved).
5. A resolved pair's next breach opens a NEW incident linked via `prior_incident_id` (reopen chain).

**Endpoints + authz:** `GET /api/v1/incidents` (filter asset/suite/state) · `GET /incidents/{id}` (+evidence) · `POST /incidents/{id}/ack` · `/resolve`. Visibility derives from suite grants (`accessible_suite_ids`, same as #760); read=`view`, act=`edit`; 404-no-leak (unknown and ungranted return byte-identical bodies); workspace-admin sees/acts everywhere.

**Evidence card (layer 1, deterministic, existing-data-only, PII-safe):** `generated_at`, `check`, `asset`, `failing_result{status,metric_value,observed_value,expected_value}` (**never `sample_failures`**), `metric_trend` (last 10 readings), `sibling_checks`, `upstream_pipeline_run{…,duration_seconds,delay_seconds_vs_history}` (via `triggered_by` correlation, null for manual), `downstream_blast_radius` (lineage BFS), `profile_diff: null` (documented — needs live introspection). Snapshotted at open, refreshed per occurrence.

**Publisher payload change:** `RunReport` gained `incidents: list[IncidentCard]` (default `[]`; `IncidentCard{incident_id, check_id, check_name, status, occurrence_count, is_new, evidence}`). `build_run_report` populates one card per breaching check with an active incident; the fail-soft `sync_incidents_for_run` hook runs in `run_suite` **before** alert dispatch, so alerts stay per-result but reference the open incident.

<result>Done. Issue #762 is built and committed on `feature/issue-762-lineage-provider` (commit `8f6a455d`), working tree clean. Not pushed, no PR opened.

## What shipped

**The `LineageProvider` seam** — `backend/app/lineage/provider.py`
```python
class LineageProvider(Protocol):
    provider: str
    def get_lineage(self, *, namespace: str, name: str, depth: int) -&gt; LineageGraph: ...
```
- **Node-kind contract** (the #762-comment "downstream isn't always a table"): `LineageGraph.nodes: dict[str, LineageNode]` where each `LineageNode(node_id, kind, namespace, name)` carries `LineageNodeKind` = `DATASET | JOB | BI_REPORT | DASHBOARD | UNKNOWN`. `coerce()` is total — an unmodelled catalog kind maps to `UNKNOWN`, never crashes, so a Power-BI report/dashboard round-trips the moment a capable provider lands. Edges are directed `(upstream_node_id, downstream_node_id)`. Docstring names the deferred impls (DataHub / OpenMetadata SDK — ADR 0031 blocked / Purview).

**Marquez reference impl** — `backend/app/lineage/marquez.py`
- `GET {MARQUEZ_URL}/api/v1/lineage?nodeId=dataset:{ns}:{name}&amp;depth=N` (verified response shape against Marquez 0.50.0 `Node.java`/`Edge.java`: `{graph:[{id,type,data,inEdges,outEdges}]}`, edges are `{origin,destination}` directed origin→downstream). Identity read from node `data` (never by splitting the id string — OL namespaces contain `:`).
- Config keys (emitter's Settings pattern, dark by default): `LINEAGE_PROVIDER=marquez` + `MARQUEZ_URL`. Fail-soft: 5s timeout, depth clamp [1,20], node cap 10000, tolerant parse (empty graph on any failure). Uses the repo's module-level `httpx.get` — **no new dependency**.

**connection_id decision + migration** — `1a2b3c4d5e6f_lineage_edges_nullable_connection.py` (chained off current head `f0a1b2c3d4e5`; **`alembic heads` = single head before and after**; re-chain note added in case #775's `c4e5a6b7d8f9` merges first). A catalog pull has no orchestration connection, so I made `lineage_edges.connection_id` **nullable** (additive/backward-compatible — the model docstring already anticipated this) and added a **partial unique index** `(upstream, downstream, source) WHERE connection_id IS NULL`. Postgres treats NULLs as distinct in a plain unique constraint, so without the partial index a NULL-connection upsert would duplicate every refresh. Validated up→down→up on a fresh DB, and introspected the result: `connection_id` nullable, both the full constraint and the partial index present, FKs intact.

**Coexistence (no duplication):** pulled edges = `source='marquez'`, `connection_id=NULL`, dedup on the partial index, prune scoped to `(source='marquez', connection_id IS NULL)` — **dbt edges (non-NULL connection_id, full unique constraint) are never touched**. The same physical A→B pair can exist as both a dbt row and a marquez row; the source-agnostic blast-radius walk spans both and dedups.

**Refresh trigger** — `refresh_lineage_pull` daily beat task (`pull.py::get_lineage_provider` gate → `refresh_pulled_edges`), dark unless configured, also callable on-demand. Daily (not liveness) chosen to mirror ADR 0034's "pulled, never built / freshness bounded by poll cadence" posture — same low-urgency cadence as the orphan/retention sweeps.

**Compose** — opt-in profile: `docker compose --profile lineage up` starts Marquez + its own trust-auth Postgres (2 containers). Does **not** start on plain `docker compose up` (verified via `docker compose config --services` with and without the profile). No committed credential (trust auth; the JDBC password is env-substituted). Stalled-release risk (0.50.0, 2024-10) recorded in compose, docs, and ADR 0034.

**Docs:** `docs/orchestration.md` gained a `LineageProvider` subsection + the emit→Marquez→pull round-trip runbook (the live round-trip is documented as a manual/compose step, not CI). ADR 0034 decision-3 updated with the #762 build note + nullable-connection scope shift.

**Deferred (not built), per docstrings:** DataHub, OpenMetadata (SDK blocked by ADR 0031), Purview.

## Tests + gates
- `test_provider.py` (seam/coerce totality, frozen DTOs, Protocol conformance), `test_marquez.py` (contract + adversarial: garbage/non-dict/missing-graph payloads, non-200, transport error, malformed/unknown-kind nodes, cyclic graphs, dangling edges, missing namespace, nested-id fallback, node-cap truncation — all mocked httpx, no live Marquez), `test_pull.py` (DB-backed round-trip with a canned real-shaped graph, dbt-coexistence-no-duplication, idempotent re-pull, prune-vs-dbt-safety, identity-less-node drop, fail-open, factory gate), `test_lineage_pull_task.py` (beat wiring, dark-path no-op).
- **New modules: provider 100%, marquez 96%, pull 98%** (all ≥80).
- **Gates green:** black `--check`, ruff, mypy (app + tests), bandit (no issues), and the **full backend suite: 1869 passed, 1 skipped, 98.34% total coverage** (≥80 gate met). Migration up/down/up verified on a throwaway Postgres (isolated container on :5433 — the running stack was never touched; container removed).

## PBI-scenario note
The seam now makes catalog-pulled BI nodes *representable*: a `LineageProvider` returns a graph whose downstream nodes carry a kind, so a report/dashboard is a first-class node rather than an assumed table. What remains for a real Purview/DataHub impl: (1) a new `LineageProvider` subclass hitting that catalog's lineage API and mapping its URNs → OL `namespace/name` + a node kind; (2) the pull-to-cache step currently only materializes **DATASET** endpoints into `assets`/`lineage_edges` (jobs are collapsed through) — surfacing a BI node as a first-class downstream asset needs the `assets` model to grow a kind column (a future migration), at which point `pull._collapse_to_datasets` widens to keep BI endpoints. No seam or query change is needed for that — the graph already carries the kind.

## Caveats
- The compose Marquez DB password default (`marquez-dev-unused`, trust-auth, env-substituted) can't be scanned locally (betterleaks isn't installed here); it's low-entropy and not a functioning secret, but CI's secret scan is the first place it'll be exercised.
- Job-collapse handles the single-non-dataset-hop bipartite case Marquez emits (dataset→job→dataset) plus direct dataset→dataset; multi-job chains aren't contracted (documented).
- The live emitter→Marquez→pull round-trip is a manual/compose verification (documented), not CI — CI covers the pull-parse-upsert path via the canned-response fixture.</result>

# Evidence report: dbt-manifest lineage — Unity Catalog / Databricks (live)

**Verdict: PASS end-to-end.** The dbt-manifest lineage path works for the `dbt-databricks` adapter with byte-identical asset identity unification against a UC suite. No product code changed; no bug found (one environment observation below).

## Environment used
- **Live Databricks Free Edition**: host `dbc-4492dde4-090c.cloud.databricks.com`, warehouse `b6403b6e3734f0ce`, catalog `dataq_retail` (schemas raw/silver/gold/reference). PAT fetched inline from Key Vault `dataq-app-kv-aw6laj` secret `conn-unity-catalog-retail` — never printed, filed, or passed as argv.
- **dbt**: throwaway venv in scratchpad — `dbt-core 1.11.12` + `dbt-databricks 1.12.2`. Manifest `dbt_schema_version = v12` (DataQ's target version).
- **Local DataQ stack**: docker-compose (api/worker/postgres/redis all up), `AUTH_DEV_BYPASS=true` (dev-bypass user is workspace admin).
- Probe project: `~/Coding/Python/DataQ-harness/dbt/uc_lineage_probe/` (separate from the Snowflake `dataq_lineage` project, as instructed; removed at cleanup).

## Models built (live, against `dataq_retail`)
Real `dbt build` → PASS=2, created two views in Databricks:
- `stg_sales_events` ← `source('raw','sales_events')` (existing UC table)
- `mart_sales_by_channel` ← `ref('stg_sales_events')`

Manifest confirmed `adapter_type: databricks`; `parent_map` chain: `raw.sales_events → stg_sales_events → mart_sales_by_channel`.

## Computed OpenLineage namespace
`unitycatalog://dbc-4492dde4-090c.cloud.databricks.com` — pinned via the dbt connection's `lineage_namespace` (matches exactly what the UC suite resolver derives from `workspace_url`). This is the ADR-0034 UC identity (`unitycatalog://&lt;workspace host&gt;`, `catalog.schema.table` lower-folded).

## Ingestion
Registered dbt connection (`artifacts_uri=file:///tmp/dbt-uc` — base prefix per the #769 footgun; `jobs=["uc_probe"]`; artifacts staged into the worker at `/tmp/dbt-uc/uc_probe/latest/manifest.json`). Triggered `refresh_dbt_lineage(connection_id, "uc_probe")` in the worker:
```
dbt_lineage_refreshed  nodes=3  edges=2  namespace=unitycatalog://dbc-4492dde4-090c.cloud.databricks.com
RESULT: refreshed
```

`lineage_edges` (source='dbt'):
```
dataq_retail.raw.sales_events                    -&gt; dataq_retail.analytics_probe_analytics_probe.stg_sales_events
...analytics_probe_analytics_probe.stg_sales_events -&gt; ...analytics_probe_analytics_probe.mart_sales_by_channel
```

## Identity unification — PASS
Sequence proves a single shared row:
1. UC suite (`catalog=dataq_retail, schema=raw, table=sales_events` on `uc-lakehouse`, repointed to the real host) stamped asset **`703a3a7c`** — `namespace=unitycatalog://dbc-4492dde4-090c.cloud.databricks.com`, `name=dataq_retail.raw.sales_events`, `connection_id=uc-lakehouse`, `env=uat`.
2. The dbt refresh's source node resolved to **the same asset id `703a3a7c`** (namespace+name byte-identical), with `connection_id` **still `uc-lakehouse`** — i.e. `preserve_provenance=True` reused the suite's row rather than creating a dbt-owned duplicate or flipping provenance. The two dbt models became new rows owned by the dbt connection. This is exactly the "join, not a mapping layer" property ADR 0034 claims.

## Blast radius — PASS
Exercising the real `edges.downstream_assets` / `upstream_assets` code path:
- `downstream_assets(sales_events)` → `[stg_sales_events, mart_sales_by_channel]`
- `upstream_assets(mart_sales_by_channel)` → `[stg_sales_events, sales_events]`

## Issues filed
None — no product defect found. One **environment observation** (not a code bug, so no issue per policy): the local dev Postgres was 3 migrations behind `head` (missing `assets.description`, incidents table, nullable `lineage_edges.connection_id`). The blast-radius BFS logic worked (it discovered the correct downstream ids), but the final `select(Asset)` ORM hydration errored on the missing `assets.description` column until I ran `alembic upgrade head`. The code is correct and the migration exists; the local stack simply hadn't been upgraded. Worth a routine `docker compose run --rm migrate` on this box before further verification work.

## Cleanup performed
- Dropped the live Databricks probe schemas `dataq_retail.analytics_probe_analytics_probe` + `analytics_probe` (CASCADE); confirmed raw/silver/gold/reference intact.
- Deleted the probe UC suite and the probe dbt connection via API (dbt-connection delete cascaded its `lineage_edges` — 0 orphans verified).
- Deleted the 3 probe asset rows; restored `uc-lakehouse` to its original placeholder `workspace_url`/`warehouse_id`.
- Removed staged artifacts from the worker (`/tmp/dbt-uc`) and the throwaway `uc_lineage_probe` dbt project from the harness.
- Left in place (intentional, correct state): the 3 applied migrations bringing the local DB to `head`; the original `lineage-dbt-project` (Snowflake) dbt connection.

Net: local stack and live workspace returned to pre-verification state, minus the migration catch-up which was a needed fix.</result>

## What changed

**Finding 1 (pandas-path wording + calibration dead-end) — fixed in the hint, the docs cheat-sheet, and the source comment block:**
- The pandas-path hint now reads:
  &gt; *"Compares pandas dtypes or Python value type names — numerics report `int64`/`float64` (integer columns containing NULLs report `float64`); string columns on Unity Catalog and CSV reads are `object` dtype, so `object` or `str` both pass, while Parquet/Iceberg reads are Arrow-backed and can report different names. Dry-run to calibrate: a failing result's observed_value shows the expected dtype — but if Observed shows "—", your guess fell to GX's row-wise compare; use `object` or a Python value type name (full cheat-sheet in the check-authoring docs)."*
- The docs cheat-sheet (`docs/datasources-checks.md`) now explains GX's actual two-phase behavior (exact dtype match first; row-wise value-type fallback only when the dtype is `object` and `type_` isn't `object`/`object_`/`O`), marks UC/CSV as not-Arrow-backed vs Parquet/Iceberg as Arrow-backed in the table, and the calibration tip is honestly qualified: exact expected string on Snowflake + Arrow-backed sources; on UC/CSV a wrong value-type guess fails with **no** observed value (Observed renders "—") — the fix is `object` or the Python value type name, not string-hunting.
- The Snowflake/SQL hint is unchanged (it was verified accurate).

**Finding 2 (nullable-int upcast) — added in both places:** the hint carries "(integer columns containing NULLs report `float64`)" and the doc table rows for UC and CSV both carry the bolded NULLs-upcast caveat; the prose bullet explains it's `pd.read_sql_table`/`pd.read_csv` doing the upcast.

**Tests:** RTL assertions re-anchored on stable substrings of the new wording (`` `object` or `str` both pass ``, `` NULLs report `float64` ``, `row-wise`) rather than full-string matches; the stale `/not \`object\`/` assertions removed.

**Gate results (frontend only — no backend files touched):** prettier clean, eslint clean, `pnpm test:coverage` — 65 files / 459 tests all passing, lines 89% (≥80 gate met).</result>

## What changed per finding

1. **HIGH — OwnerBlock /me race → mount-gating.** `AssetDetailBody` now renders `{isAdmin &amp;&amp; &lt;OwnerBlock …/&gt;}`; `OwnerBlock` lost its `canEdit` prop and does an unconditional `useAsyncData(listAdminUsers)` on mount. When `/me` resolves and `useIsWorkspaceAdmin()` flips false→true, the block mounts fresh and the fetch fires — no stale closure over a pre-resolution `canEdit`, no dead Select, no raw-UUID owner. The non-admin-never-fetches guarantee is now structural (component never mounts).

2. **MEDIUM — truncation honesty in AssetHealthLead.** New `LIST_CAP = 200` constant; when `assets.length &gt;= LIST_CAP` the widget renders "Showing the first 200 assets — open Assets for the full list." below the tiles (with a comment noting the tiles are a lower bound at the cap). No multi-page aggregation, per instruction.

3. **LOW-MED — attention preview severity ordering.** Added `SEVERITY_RANK` (critical 3 &gt; fail 2 &gt; warn 1 &gt; operational-run-failure 0) and the attention list is `.filter(needsAttention).sort(worst-first)` before `slice(0, 5)` — stable sort preserves the backend's alphabetical order within a tier.

4. **LOW — OwnerBlock error state.** `state.status === 'error'` now renders "The user list is unavailable right now." inline (mirroring the AssetHealthLead pattern) and disables the Reassign button — no silently-empty picker.

5. **LOW — tests.** Reinstated `expect(listAdminUsers).not.toHaveBeenCalled()` in the non-admin test; mock isolation hardened by clearing mocks in `beforeEach` as well as `afterEach` (any late-recorded call between tests is wiped before counting). Added the **/me-race recovery test** — the harness *can* express it: extracted a `pageTree(isAdmin)` builder and used RTL `rerender(pageTree(true))` after asserting zero calls at `isAdmin=false`; the test asserts the fetch fires exactly once when adminness appears. Also added the user-list error-state test (message shown + button disabled), the severity-sort test (critical/fail lead the preview, trailing warns fold into "+2 more"), and truncation at-cap / below-cap tests.

## Summary

Implemented issue #725 (request rate limiting on every public surface) per the approved plan. **PR #783** — https://github.com/TheurgicDuke771/DataQ/pull/783 — milestone set to "v1.1 Week 3 — Azure wind-down + local-first posture". Single commit **`85849fa1`**.

### What was built
- **`backend/app/core/rate_limit.py`** (new): innermost `@app.middleware` fixed-window (60s) limiter, window index baked into the Redis key (`rl:{cls}:{key}:{window}`, no EXPIRE race), one INCR+EXPIRE pipeline via the already-present `redis.asyncio` — **no new dependency**. `RateLimitStore` Protocol seam with `RedisStore` (fail-open → `None` on any error, warn-once-per-window) and `InMemoryStore` (test-only, injectable clock). Classes: `webhook` (per-IP, even with bearer), `default` (per-`sha256(token)[:32]`), `unauth` (per-IP). Raw token never keyed/logged; `/healthz`+`OPTIONS` exempt; client IP = last XFF hop; 429 carries `Retry-After` + `X-RateLimit-*` + `detail.retry_after_seconds`. Reuses `auth._bearer_token`; `set_store_for_testing`/`reset_rate_limit_state` mirror the `secrets.py` reset pattern.
- **`main.py`**: registered first (innermost) with the comment explaining CORS/request_id/mount coverage.
- **`config.py`**: 4 `RATE_LIMIT_*` fields.
- **`conftest.py`**: `RATE_LIMIT_ENABLED=false` suite default + `reset_rate_limit_state()` in the autouse reset fixture.
- **Tests** (27, all passing): `backend/tests/core/test_rate_limit.py` (policy, client-IP, both stores, warn-once) + `backend/tests/api/test_rate_limiting.py` (all 10 TestClient cases incl. `/mcp` coverage, fail-open, window reset, XFF keying).
- **Docs**: ADR 0035 + index row, `deploy/README.md` env rows, `.env.app.example` section, `docs/rest-api.md` 429, `docs/progress.md` snapshot + Open PRs.

### Gate (local, mirrors CI)
- `black --check backend/` clean (280 files); `ruff check backend/` clean.
- `mypy backend/app/` and `mypy backend/tests/` — no issues.
- `bandit -c pyproject.toml -r backend/app/` — 0 issues.
- `pytest backend/tests/` — **1974 passed, 0 failed**, coverage **98.30%** (gate ≥80). New module `rate_limit.py` at 95% (only live-Redis-only lines uncovered).
- Pre-commit hooks (betterleaks etc.) passed on commit; no `--no-verify`.

### Deviations from the plan (2)

- **Point 5 (test cleanup):** `set_store_for_testing` is set in the `limiter`/`failopen_client`/window fixtures with NO per-fixture teardown, but the autouse `_reset_caches` (conftest.py) is instantiated FIRST (autouse) so it finalizes LAST — calling `reset_rate_limit_state()` after each test clears `_store_override`, `_redis_client`, and the warn stamp. `_now` monkeypatches auto-revert. No store leakage across tests.
- **Point 4 (MCP token budget):** each MCP tool call is one HTTP POST through the middleware (INCR once); the streamable-http SSE GET is one long-held request = one INCR. All MCP requests from a session carry the same bearer → one `tok:` bucket at 300/min. <result>I have enough to finalize. My analysis of the middleware ordering, conftest, disabled-path, and 429 collisions is complete.

Verified facts:
- Middleware request-arrival order (branch): `request_id → reject_nul → CORS → rate_limit → router`. The three pre-existing middlewares keep their relative order; rate_limit is innermost as claimed. NUL-rejection still runs before routing, request_id still wraps everything, CORS still wraps errors — those existing invariants are preserved.
- Disabled path is truly zero-touch (early `return await call_next(request)` before any header/response mutation; only a cached `get_settings()` call).
- No existing `429`/`Retry-After`/`rate_limited` usage anywhere → no collision. No error-code registry to update.
- conftest change is purely additive; no test asserts on the Settings field-set or on `RATE_LIMIT_*`. `_bearer_token` is header-only and cannot raise.
- All three orchestrator webhook routes share the `/api/v1/orchestration/events/` prefix → all land in one per-IP `webhook` bucket.

## Verdict: CONFIRMED

**Exact code path** (`backend/app/core/rate_limit.py`):

1. Middleware is registered on the parent app as an HTTP middleware (`main.py:108`), running the request *before* auth — auth is a route dependency (`_bearer_token` at `auth.py:87` is invoked downstream). So the middleware sees an **unvalidated** bearer.
2. `_bearer_token` (`auth.py:76-82`) extracts the raw token from the `Authorization: Bearer …` header only — attacker-controlled, need not be valid, cannot be query-smuggled.
3. `_resolve_policy` (`rate_limit.py:200-205`): non-webhook + `bearer is not None` → `("default", rate_limit_authenticated_per_minute, f"tok:{sha256(bearer)[:32]}")`. The per-IP unauth branch (line 205) is only reached when `bearer is None`.
4. `rate_limit_middleware` (line 242) increments `rl:default:tok:{digest}:{window}`.

An attacker sending a fresh random bearer per request from one IP mints a new `tok:` digest each time → every bucket sees `count=1 ≤ 300` → never 429. The per-IP unauth cap (120/min) is structurally unreachable for any bearer-carrying request. This delivers: (a) unbounded volumetric bypass of the limiter's core purpose, (b) unthrottled 401 credential-guessing at the auth layer, (c) Redis key-cardinality blowup — one new 120s-TTL key per distinct token, unbounded within a window. Both finders are correct.

## Evaluation of the proposed fix

**Does it close the bypass?** Yes. Rotated tokens from one IP all increment the *same* `ipall:{ip}` bucket, so the per-IP ceiling (default 600/min) trips regardless of token churn. This is the correct architecture: you cannot key on the bearer as an identity until it's validated, and you *want* to throttle invalid-bearer guessing — so a token-independent per-IP volumetric ceiling applied **before** auth is exactly the right tool. Moving rate-limiting after auth (so only valid tokens bucket) is not viable — it would leave the guessing attack entirely unthrottled and can't cover `/mcp`.

**New failure modes — assessed:**
- **4-command pipeline round trips:** Confirmed single round trip. `redis.asyncio` `pipeline(transaction=True)` buffers `INCR,EXPIRE,INCR,EXPIRE` and flushes them in one `execute()` (wrapped MULTI/EXEC). No extra RTT vs today's 2-command pipeline. This is why the `incr_windows` protocol change is justified over calling `incr_window` twice (which would double RTT on the *common* authed path — frontend polling).
- **Exclude webhook from the ceiling:** Yes, correct, and the proposal already does (ceiling only for the bearer/non-webhook `default` class). Webhooks are already IP-capped at 30/min and originate from orchestrators (ADF/Airflow/dbt) that may collapse to one egress IP; folding them into a second per-IP bucket would double-account and risk starving legitimate callbacks.
- **NAT / collapsed-IP topology — the real risk, but not new.** The ceiling's safety rests entirely on `_client_ip` (lines 169-186) yielding the true client IP. In this deployment the api has *internal* ingress reached only via the frontend nginx proxy, so `request.client.host` is always the nginx pod IP; correctness depends on the rightmost XFF hop being the real peer. If XFF is ever absent/garbage for a traffic class, `_client_ip` returns the nginx IP or `"unknown"`, and **all** authenticated prod traffic collapses into one `ipall:` bucket → a 600/min cap on the entire deployment. Crucially, **this dependency already exists** for the current unauth per-IP bucket; the fix does not introduce it, but it *widens the blast radius* from unauth-only to all authenticated traffic. Note also any extra proxy hop (ACA ingress in front of nginx) could make the rightmost hop an infra IP — worth confirming the nginx XFF chain, but that's a pre-existing concern.
- **600 default for real traffic:** At ~45 req/min per polling browser, 600 gives ~13 concurrent users behind a shared office NAT before the combined ceiling bites, plus MCP-agent headroom. For single-tenant DataQ this is *probably* fine, but it is tight for a corporate all-behind-one-NAT deployment. Since it's a config field, keep it configurable and document the NAT math; I'd lean to a more generous default (e.g. 1200) — the ceiling only needs to be well below "abuse," not near "legit peak."

## Minimal correct implementation shape

1. **Protocol** (`RateLimitStore`): `async def incr_windows(self, keys: Sequence[str]) -&gt; list[int] | None`. Return counts aligned to input order; any store error → `None` (single fail-open signal for the whole batch). Implement in `RedisStore` (one `transaction=True` pipeline, N×`INCR`+`EXPIRE`), `InMemoryStore` (increment each key independently under the existing prune). Update `set_store_for_testing` typing.
2. **Config** (`config.py`): add `rate_limit_ip_per_minute: int = 600` (consider 1200). Add to the env-var reference doc (#468) and `.env.app.example`.
3. **Middleware**: for the `default` class only, build both keys — `rl:default:tok:{digest}:{window}` and a new-class `rl:ipall:ip:{ip}:{window}` — call `incr_windows([tok_key, ip_key])`; 429 if `tok_count &gt; authenticated_limit` **OR** `ip_count &gt; ip_limit`. Webhook and unauth stay single-key (each already IP-capped on its own bucket, so no separate ceiling needed — and dropping the bearer only demotes an attacker to the *lower* unauth `ip:` cap, so both paths remain IP-bounded). On 429, set `X-RateLimit-Limit` to whichever limit was exceeded (prefer the token limit if both). Fail-open unchanged (`None` → allow + warn-once).
4. **Tests to add**: (a) **regression** — rotate a fresh bearer per request from one IP → 429 after the ip ceiling (proves the bypass is closed); (b) two distinct tokens, same IP → counted together against `ipall:`; (c) single legit token still capped at `authenticated_per_minute` (token bucket intact); (d) webhook-with-bearer path **not** counted against `ipall:`; (e) `incr_windows` returns list aligned to keys, and `None` (store error) → request allowed for both dimensions; (f) `Retry-After`/`X-RateLimit-Limit` correct when the ceiling (not the token bucket) is the limiter; (g) `InMemoryStore.incr_windows` increments keys independently.

**Bottom line:** the proposed dual-key ceiling is the right fix and I found no simpler correct alternative — endorse it as specified. The one refinement worth carrying into the PR (or a filed follow-up) is the `_client_ip`/XFF collapse risk now that the ceiling extends per-IP dependence to *all* authenticated traffic: verify the nginx XFF chain and add a test pinning the missing-XFF behavior, and reconsider whether 600 is generous enough for the intended deployment.</result>

<result>## Verdicts — PR #783 rate limiting middleware

**1. Lazy Redis client init race — REFUTED.**
`_get_redis_client()` (rate_limit.py:67-79) is a *synchronous* function with no `await` inside it. Under asyncio's single-threaded cooperative scheduler, a sync function with no yield point cannot be interleaved by another task — the check-then-set on `_redis_client` runs atomically to completion once started. There is no window for two tasks to both observe `None` and both construct a client. Separately, even if this were somehow re-introduced with an `await` inside, `redis.asyncio.from_url()` builds a `Redis`/`ConnectionPool` object lazily — no socket opens until the first command executes (`ConnectionPool.get_connection()` on first `.execute()`) — so an orphaned client object would never hold a live socket unless it had already served a request. No fix needed; not worth a lock. **Severity: won't-fix-document** (optionally add a one-line comment noting sync-no-await ⇒ no race, to preempt future reviewer déjà vu).

**2. EXPIRE on every hit — REFUTED (not a problem).**
`docker-compose.yml:33` pins `redis:7-alpine` for local/dev, and `deploy/terraform/azure/redis.tf:43` pins the identical `redis:7-alpine` for the Azure Container App — so EXPIRE NX is actually available everywhere DataQ runs today. But the unconditional EXPIRE isn't a bug to begin with: INCR+EXPIRE already ride one pipelined round trip (`transaction=True`), so there's no extra network cost from sending both; EXPIRE is deliberately "pure GC, never the limit boundary" per the module docstring and ADR 0035, since the window is baked into the key. Switching to NX buys nothing (same round-trip count) and adds a Redis-version dependency for zero benefit — the current design is actually the simpler, more version-portable choice. **Severity: won't-fix-document** (already documented in the module docstring and ADR 0035 §Decision).

**3. No circuit breaker for slow-but-alive Redis — PLAUSIBLE, low severity.**
Accurate as stated: `socket_timeout=0.2` / `socket_connect_timeout=0.5` (rate_limit.py:76-77) bounds the per-request tax during a degraded-but-alive Redis to ~0.2s (or up to ~0.7s if the pooled connection needs to reconnect), and every request pays it until the outage clears — there's no breaker to short-circuit repeat attempts within a window. That said: the bound is small and deterministic, fail-open already prevents a hard-down API, the warn-once-per-window log already surfaces sustained degradation, and ADR 0035 explicitly chose availability-over-enforcement and a 30-line implementation over adding complexity/deps (rejecting `slowapi`/`limits` for exactly this kind of reason). A breaker is legitimate future hardening but not proportionate to this PR's scope. **Severity: file-issue** (post-v1 backlog candidate — a lightweight "N consecutive timeouts → skip Redis for the rest of the window" breaker), not a PR blocker.

**4. BaseHTTPMiddleware wrapping /mcp streamable-http — REFUTED as a new risk.**
main.py already runs `/mcp` through two `@app.middleware("http")` (= `BaseHTTPMiddleware`) layers — `reject_nul_in_url_middleware` and `request_id_middleware` — before this PR; `rate_limit_middleware` is a third of the same kind, registered innermost per the ADR's ordering rationale (main.py:103-108). Adding a third BaseHTTPMiddleware layer is quantitatively more overhead but not a qualitatively new risk class: it's the same buffering/anyio-task-group mechanics the other two already exercise against the live `/mcp` mount, which is validated end-to-end in prod (#550 client-config E2E, the live MCP protocol smoke in the #531 lane). Installed Starlette is **1.2.1** (`backend/requirements.txt` pins `fastapi==0.138.2`, which pulls it transitively) — well past the older BaseHTTPMiddleware streaming/cancellation footguns from the ~0.34-and-earlier line, so there's no version-relevant landmine here. `test_mcp_mount_is_covered` (`backend/tests/api/test_rate_limiting.py:127`) confirms the 429 path works through the stack. **Severity: won't-fix-document** (optionally note in the PR/ADR that this is the third, not first, BaseHTTPMiddleware over `/mcp`, and it rides the same already-live-validated mechanism).

No fix-in-PR changes recommended for any of the four. Only item 3 warrants a tracked follow-up issue; the rest are either refuted outright or already adequately documented in ADR 0035 / the module docstring.</result>

## VERIFICATION REPORT — PR #783 rate-limit `_client_ip` XFF handling

### 1. What each hop does to X-Forwarded-For

**(a) nginx — APPENDS.** `frontend/nginx.conf.template` sets `proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-For $proxy_add_x_forwarded_for;` on all three proxied locations (`/api/` L66, `/healthz` L82, `/mcp` L96). `$proxy_add_x_forwarded_for` = incoming XFF + `,` + `$remote_addr` (nginx's TCP peer). So nginx never replaces; it appends the IP of whoever connected to it (in ACA, that peer is the public-ingress envoy's internal source, not the real client).

**(b) ACA ingress (Envoy) — APPENDS, at BOTH hops.** ACA's managed ingress is Envoy with `use_remote_address`, which appends the immediate downstream peer to XFF. This happens at the **public** ingress in front of `dataq-app-frontend` (appends the real client IP) *and* at the **internal** ingress in front of `dataq-app-api` (`external_enabled=false`, containerapps.tf L107 — still an envoy ingress; in-CAE traffic from nginx traverses it, and it appends the **frontend nginx pod IP**).

Full prod chain, browser sending no XFF:
```
Client → [public envoy: append C] → nginx → [internal envoy: append N] → uvicorn
```
- public envoy appends `C` (real client)          → `"C"`
- nginx `$proxy_add_x_forwarded_for` appends `E1` (public-ingress internal src) → `"C, E1"`
- internal envoy appends `N` (nginx pod IP)         → `"C, E1, N"`

**uvicorn sees `XFF = "C, E1, N"` — rightmost = `N` (nginx pod IP), a single shared infra value.** Real client `C` is at index `len−3`.

**(c) docker-compose — two dev paths, neither uses nginx:**
- Dev (`docker-compose.yml`): browser → Vite dev server `:3000` (proxy `/api`→`:8000`) **or** browser → api `:8000` directly (the CLAUDE.md curl smoke). Vite's proxy config (`vite.config.ts` L23) has **no `xfwd`**, so http-proxy does **not** append XFF → api sees no XFF → `_client_ip` falls back to `request.client.host`. Direct `:8000` hits likewise have no XFF → socket peer. The candidate's "compose = client → nginx → api" only holds for `docker-compose.ghcr.yml` (the prebuilt-nginx path), where nginx does append and rightmost IS the client.

### 2. Verdict on the prod-ACA collapse claim: **CONFIRMED**

The rightmost XFF entry uvicorn sees in prod is definitively `N` (the frontend nginx pod IP), **not** the client. With one frontend replica, every browser request, every unauth request, and every external webhook (ADF/Airflow POST to `&lt;frontend&gt;/api/v1/orchestration/events/…` — same public→nginx→internal chain) collapses to one `ip:{N}` bucket. So all unauth traffic shares one 120/min cap and all webhook senders share one 30/min cap. The `default` (`tok:`) class is unaffected (keyed on `sha256(bearer)`), which is why the ADR gets away with it — but the per-IP classes are effectively single-bucket. (The ADR §"Threat model" already *documents and accepts* this collapse; PR #783 as committed still ships rightmost-XFF and does **not** contain the `rate_limit_xff_trusted_hops` field — confirmed absent from `config.py`. So this is evaluating a proposed remediation.)

Caveat on exactness: the *depth* (3) is the expected trusted-append count but should be confirmed by logging one live XFF — don't hard-assume it. The qualitative claim (rightmost = infra, not client) is certain regardless of exact N.

### 3. Evaluating the proposed fix (`hops`-from-right)

`entries[max(0, len(entries) − hops)]`, default `hops=1`:

- **Compose ghcr (1 append):** `hops=1` → rightmost → client. **Correct.** Spoof-safe: a client-supplied XFF only grows the left, nginx's append is always rightmost.
- **Compose dev (Vite / direct :8000):** no XFF → falls to `request.client.host`. **Correct** (dev-only anyway).
- **ACA (N=3):** `hops=1` picks `N` (nginx pod IP) → **still collapses.** Default `1` is **NOT acceptable-degraded for ACA — it reproduces the exact bug being fixed.** The correct ACA value is **`hops=3`** (real client is the 3rd-from-right = the entry the *public* envoy appended; everything to its right is trusted infra, everything to its left is client-spoofable). Counting-from-right is spoof-robust *when actual chain depth == hops*: a client prepending fake entries pushes them left and they're ignored.
- **Direct-hit spoofing:**
  - *Prod:* api is internal-ingress, unreachable from the internet — but an in-CAE caller hitting the internal ingress directly gets `XFF = "spoofed…, theirPodIP"`; with the wrong depth they can set `entries[len−hops]` to a chosen value. Requires an already-compromised in-env position; effect limited to rate-bucket evasion/poisoning. Low but non-zero.
  - *Local dev (`:8000` exposed):* an attacker sending `X-Forwarded-For: 1.2.3.4` with `hops=1` gets `entries[0]="1.2.3.4"` — **full control of their bucket key**: rotate fake IPs → unlimited unauth/webhook buckets (evade), or send a victim's IP → exhaust the victim's bucket (poison/DoS). This is the classic "trust XFF without a proxy" footgun. Same exposure exists in the *current* rightmost code, so the fix doesn't regress it — but it doesn't close it either.

**Footgun in the fallback rule:** "fewer entries than hops → `entries[0]`" is the *least* safe branch — when a request arrives with a **shorter** chain than expected (a direct/fewer-proxy hit), `entries[0]` is the most client-controlled value. Safer: when `len(entries) &lt; hops`, fall back to `request.client.host` (the unspoofable socket peer), since a too-short chain means the request didn't traverse the trusted proxies and its XFF is untrustworthy. Keep the existing `_is_ip` validation + `client.host` final fallback on the selected entry.

### 4. Simpler robust alternative + minimal recommendation

**Trusted-proxy CIDR walk** (what Starlette `ProxyHeadersMiddleware` / uvicorn `--forwarded-allow-ips` / werkzeug behave like): walk XFF right-to-left, skip entries in a trusted set (RFC1918 / the CAE subnet), return the first *untrusted* entry = the real client. More robust than a fixed count — tolerates variable depth and, critically, refuses to trust XFF on a direct hit (peer not trusted → use socket). Downside: ACA internal pod IPs come from a dynamic range, so the trusted set is a "trust all private ranges" heuristic that mis-handles a legitimately private-sourced client (internal webhook). For DataQ (Azure winding down, per-IP classes are an accepted coarse backstop) the CIDR maintenance isn't worth it.

**Minimal correct change — recommend the `hops` approach WITH these fixes:**
1. Ship `rate_limit_xff_trusted_hops: int = 1` (correct for local/single-proxy; matches the `ProxyFix(x_for=N)` idiom).
2. Select `entries[len − hops]` **only when `len(entries) &gt;= hops`**; otherwise fall back to `request.client.host` (not `entries[0]`). Keep `_is_ip` validation → `client.host` → `"unknown"` as the tail.
3. **Set `RATE_LIMIT_XFF_TRUSTED_HOPS=3` in `deploy/terraform/azure/containerapps.tf` `local.app_env`** (api container) — **after confirming the depth by logging one live XFF**. Without this env override the PR does **not** fix the reported prod collapse; default `1` leaves ACA broken.
4. Update ADR 0035's "Threat model — the client-IP rule" section: flip the "ACA double-ingress caveat … Accepted" paragraph to "configurable trusted-hop depth, set to the measured chain; per-IP class integrity restored," and document the direct-hit caveat (only trust XFF for the exact configured proxy depth). The ADR currently *accepts* the very collapse this PR fixes — leaving it unamended would be a doc/behavior contradiction.

**Files:** `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/.claude/worktrees/agent-a37794d55abadfaeb/backend/app/core/rate_limit.py` (L169-186 `_client_ip`), `.../frontend/nginx.conf.template` (L66/82/96), `.../deploy/terraform/azure/containerapps.tf` (L106-121 internal ingress; L24-77 `app_env` — where the hops env must be added), `.../docs/adr/0035-request-rate-limiting.md` (L74-82 threat model), `.../backend/app/core/config.py` (L123-126 rate-limit settings; `xff` field not yet present).</result>

<result>## Verdicts

### CANDIDATE 1 — webhook rate limit (30/min, per-IP, shared across providers) — **CONFIRMED**, with a sharper root cause than stated

**(a) Airflow callback's exact 429 behavior** — confirmed as described. `integrations/airflow/dataq_airflow_callback.py::_post` uses stdlib `urllib.request.urlopen`, which raises `urllib.error.HTTPError` for any non-2xx (including 429). `_notify` catches it with `except urllib.error.HTTPError as exc: _LOG.warning(...)` — logs and returns. **No retry, no backoff.** `integrations/dbt/dataq_dbt_callback.py` has the identical pattern (same `_post`, same bare `except urllib.error.HTTPError` → log-and-drop). So **both self-authored callback snippets (Airflow and dbt) silently drop a 429 with zero retry.**

**(b) Does ADF/Azure Monitor retry on 429?** — Yes, and this changes the picture. Verified against Microsoft Learn docs: Azure Monitor's webhook action group explicitly treats **408, 429, 503, 504** as retryable — up to 5 retries at 5/20/5/40/5-second delays (~110s total), then backs off 15 minutes. **ADF is self-healing against a 429**; Airflow and dbt are not, because those are DataQ's own hand-rolled snippets with no retry logic. The finder's "shared by ALL three providers" framing overstates the symmetry — the real exposure is specifically the two self-authored channels.

**(c) Does the 10-min poll fallback genuinely recover both halves?** — Yes, confirmed by code, not just doc claims. `backend/app/worker/tasks.py::_poll_orchestration_runs` calls `orchestration_service.ingest_polled_runs(...)`, whose result feeds both `summary["recorded"]` (pipeline_run upsert) and `summary["triggered"]` (suite-run trigger-on-success) — the identical `ingest_event`/upsert+trigger path the webhook uses. `poll_orchestration_runs` runs every 600s (10 min, `_POLL_LOOKBACK=15min`), `recover_orchestration_gaps` every 1800s (`_GAP_RECOVERY_LOOKBACK=1h`) — both idempotent via `skip_updated_since`. So a dropped webhook degrades to **up to a 10-minute detection/trigger delay, not data loss** — real but bounded impact.

**Fix judgment (raise default 30→120/min):** the "256-bit secret" framing is a red herring either way. At 30/min (43,200/day) or 120/min (172,800/day), you're at most ~63M attempts/year against a keyspace of 2^256 (~1.15×10^77) — brute force is astronomically infeasible at *either* number; the 4x difference (≈2 bits) is noise. **Raising the default does not weaken brute-force resistance at all.** Given ADF self-heals but Airflow/dbt don't, and a realistic burst (e.g., dozens of DAGs completing in the same minute on self-hosted Airflow, potentially egressing through the same IP as the dbt build runner on shared harness infra) can plausibly exceed 30/min, the current default is too tight for the two channels that actually need it.

**Recommendation:** raise `RATE_LIMIT_WEBHOOK_PER_MINUTE` default to **120** as proposed (matches the existing `unauth` class default — a well-precedented number in this codebase, still far below `default`'s 300, preserving the "webhooks are a semi-trusted machine channel, not full API traffic" posture). Optionally file a follow-up to key the webhook bucket per-provider-path instead of the current bare `ip:{ip}` (i.e., fold `cls`/path into the key, which the `rl:{cls}:{key}:{window}` key format already technically supports since `cls="webhook"` is shared across all three routes) so a burst on one provider can't crowd out another sharing an IP — worth a GitHub issue per CONTRIBUTING rule 6, not necessarily this PR.

### CANDIDATE 2 — blanket `OPTIONS` exemption — **CONFIRMED**, and the narrowing is correct and safe

**Fetch-spec correctness:** confirmed directly against Starlette's own `CORSMiddleware.__call__` (installed version, via `inspect.getsource`): it classifies a request as a genuine preflight only when `origin is not None` **and** `method == "OPTIONS"` **and** `"access-control-request-method" in headers`. That's exactly the narrowing the finder proposed (Origin + Access-Control-Request-Method) — it's not just spec-correct, it's the identical predicate the app's own CORS layer uses.

**Does CORSMiddleware make the exemption moot when active?** No — and this is the important finding. `backend/app/main.py` registers `rate_limit_middleware` via `app.middleware("http")` *before* `CORSMiddleware` is conditionally added. Starlette's `add_middleware` does `user_middleware.insert(0, ...)` (verified via `inspect.getsource(Starlette.add_middleware)`), so registration order inverts: the **last**-registered middleware ends up **outermost**. Working through it, the actual runtime nesting is `ServerError → request_id → reject_nul → CORSMiddleware → rate_limit → ExceptionMiddleware → router` — i.e., **CORS is outside/wraps rate_limit**, matching the code comment ("a 429 still exits through CORSMiddleware"). So when CORS *is* configured, a true preflight is short-circuited by CORSMiddleware before it ever reaches `rate_limit_middleware`, making the blanket exemption redundant for that case — narrowing it would be a no-op there.

**But CORS is not configured in this deployment.** `deploy/terraform/azure/containerapps.tf:54` sets `CORS_ALLOW_ORIGINS = ""` (comment at `frontend.tf:9`: "same-origin, no CORS — the api keeps CORS_ALLOW_ORIGINS empty"), and `backend/app/main.py`'s `if _cors_origins:` guard means **`CORSMiddleware` is never added at all in prod**. In that (actual, current) configuration, `rate_limit_middleware`'s blanket `if request.method == "OPTIONS": return await call_next(request)` is the *only* logic touching OPTIONS, and it exempts every OPTIONS request — preflight-shaped or not, cross-origin or not — to every path including `/api/v1/orchestration/events/*` and `/mcp`. This is a live, unthrottled volumetric channel today, not a theoretical one.

**Legit non-preflight OPTIONS traffic check:** grepped `backend/app/`, `frontend/src/`, `integrations/` for `OPTIONS` — the only backend hit is the rate-limit exemption itself; the two frontend hits (`SharePanel.tsx`, `NotificationsPanel.tsx`) are unrelated Ant Design dropdown `options` arrays (`ALERT_ON_OPTIONS`, `PERMISSION_OPTIONS`), not HTTP methods. No MCP-transport or healthcheck use of OPTIONS found. **No legitimate non-preflight OPTIONS traffic exists in this app.**

**Recommendation:** the narrowing is correct and safe — replace the blanket check with `request.method == "OPTIONS" and "origin" in request.headers and "access-control-request-method" in request.headers`. This is strictly better in every deployment mode: a no-op when CORS is active (already short-circuited upstream) and closes a real, currently-live gap when it's not (the prod configuration today).</result>

# SECURITY-SCAN — PR #783 (issue #725, request rate limiting)

## Verdict: **GO** (from a security standpoint)

All three CI-mirrored scanners pass, no real credential shapes in the diff, and every adversarial probe either lands on an inherent-and-documented residual or a non-issue. The four prior-review fixes hold. No must-fix.

## Part 1 — Scanner results

| Scanner | Command (mirrors CI) | Result |
|---|---|---|
| **Bandit** | `bandit -c pyproject.toml -r backend/app` | **0 issues** (Low/Med/High all 0). The 5 `#nosec B105` are pre-existing in `orchestration/dbt.py` + `services/dashboard_service.py` — **none in `rate_limit.py`**. |
| **pip-audit** | `pip-audit -r backend/requirements-dev.txt` | **No known vulnerabilities.** `requirements*.txt` is byte-identical to origin/main (`git diff` empty) — **no new dependency** (ADR 0035 reuses the existing `redis==5.3.1`). |
| **betterleaks** | `ghcr.io/betterleaks/betterleaks:v1.4.1` over the full PR diff (90.6 KB) | **No leaks found.** |
| **pnpm audit** | — | **Out of scope.** `git diff --stat origin/main...HEAD` shows `frontend/` completely untouched → no lockfile change. |

**Credential-shape scan (manual, over full diff):** clean. Test bearers are all obviously synthetic — `token-AAA`, `token-BBB`, `rotate-{i}`, `solo-token`, `super-secret-token`, `sometoken`. **None `dq_live_`/`dq_sess_`-shaped.** The only `dq_sess_` hit in the diff is a doc reference in `docs/adr/README.md` describing ADR 0032, not a credential. Secret handling in the code is correct: the raw bearer is sha256-hashed before it becomes a Redis key (`rate_limit.py:230`), and the fail-open warning logs only the key **kind** (`tok`/`ip` via `key.split(":",1)[0]`), never the value (`rate_limit.py:246`). There is a dedicated regression test asserting the raw token never appears in the key (`test_raw_token_never_in_key`).

## Part 2 — Adversarial review (ranked)

The four prior fixes are present and correct: dual-key `ipall:` ceiling (`rate_limit.py:280-281,293`), hops-from-right XFF selection (`_client_ip`, :186-213), webhook cap 120 (`config.py`, default), preflight-only OPTIONS exemption (`main.py`-adjacent middleware, :258-263).

**None of the probes yield a must-fix.** Ranked by residual severity:

1. **XFF-forgery IP rotation in a hops=1 / direct-socket topology — Low, ACCEPTED/DOCUMENTED.** With `trusted_hops=1`, `_client_ip` trusts the rightmost XFF entry; an attacker who reaches the socket **directly** (bypassing the one assumed proxy) and sends a single-entry XFF gets it trusted, rotating the `ipall` ceiling freely. But: (a) the standard nginx `$proxy_add_x_forwarded_for` **appends** the real peer, so a client-supplied header is defeated as long as traffic actually transits the proxy; (b) prod runs `hops=3` with the api on **internal ingress** (containerapps.tf:52-54) — forgery there requires being *inside* the ACA trust boundary, which is the network control, not the limiter's job; (c) local `:8000` exposure is a dev-only posture. This is the inherent property of any XFF-trust scheme and is scoped in ADR 0035 §"Threat model" + "Accepted residual risks." **Used only for bucket keying, never authz** (confirmed: grep shows the sole other `client.host` consumer is audit logging in `main.py:162`, and it reads the socket peer, not XFF). Rate-limit evasion, not auth bypass. Not a blocker.

2. **Slow-but-alive Redis → global fail-open + per-request latency — Low, ACCEPTED + FOLLOW-UP FILED (#784).** `incr_windows` catches *any* exception → `None` → fail-open globally (`rate_limit.py:110-111,284-287`). A laggy Redis both disables limiting and makes every request pay up to `socket_timeout=0.2s`. This is the deliberate availability-over-enforcement trade (ADR "Fail-closed — rejected"), and the exact circuit-breaker gap is **already filed as #784**. Fail-open cannot be triggered for a single victim while enforcing others — it's global, gated on Redis reachability (shared infra the app already depends on). Not a blocker.

3. **NAT'd office throttled at the 1200/min `ipall` ceiling — Low, ACCEPTED (tunable).** A shared corporate egress IP shares one `ipall` bucket; ~20 sustained req/s of bearer traffic from one office would 429. Mitigated by generous configurable defaults (ADR: "tighten to your cadence") and per-token 300 buckets being independent. Availability trade, tune per-deployment. Worth a deploy-note; not a blocker.

4. **Pathological XFF parsing — NOT A WEAKNESS (fails safe).** Probed `a,,b`, whitespace, hostname-not-IP, `[::1]:443`, and a 10k-entry header against `_client_ip`: every malformed candidate fails `_is_ip()` and falls back to the socket peer (:208-213) — no crash, no mis-trust. Bracketed-IPv6-with-port falls back to socket peer (minor correctness miss, fail-safe — a candidate follow-up nit at most). **No DoS:** header size is bounded by the ASGI server (~16 KB h11 default), split+strip is a single O(n) pass over that bound, and `_is_ip()` is called **once** on the selected entry, not per-entry.

5. **Key injection / cardinality — NOT A WEAKNESS.** Token → 32-char sha256 hex (no separators, bounded). IP → either an `ipaddress`-validated string or the trusted socket peer or `"unknown"`. IPv6 keys contain `:`, but Redis keys are binary-safe (INCR arg, not eval) — no namespace escape, no command injection. Token-bucket cardinality is bounded by the `ipall` ceiling; IP-bucket cardinality is bounded by `EXPIRE` at 2×window GC (`rate_limit.py:105`) and, in the trusted topology, by real client count.

6. **Timing / token-validity oracle — NOT A WEAKNESS.** The limiter runs pre-auth; the 429 decision depends only on request **count**, never on token validity (no compare against any stored secret occurs). A bogus token buckets identically to a valid one. sha256 timing is validity-independent. No oracle.

7. **Webhook HMAC interplay — NOT A WEAKNESS.** The limiter short-circuits with a 429 *before* the route handler's constant-time HMAC compare ever runs (receivers use `compare_digest`, confirmed in `orchestration.py` header docs), so it cannot alter the constant-time guarantee or add a compare-timing channel. A 429 leaks only "you exceeded 120/min," nothing about HMAC validity; and the throttle *reduces* an attacker's sample budget, making timing attacks harder. The ADR's #785 (per-provider-path webhook keying) is an availability nicety, already filed.

**Middleware ordering sanity check:** `rate_limit_middleware` is registered first (`main.py:108`) = innermost, so 429s exit back through CORS + `request_id` and receive `X-Request-ID` + the structured log — matching the ADR intent and giving 429s full observability.

## Bottom line
Scanners green (Bandit 0 / pip-audit 0 / betterleaks 0; pnpm N/A). No secret is logged or committed; test creds are synthetic. The limiter **keys buckets on a spoofable value by design (accepted evasion) but never makes a security/authz decision on it, never leaks a secret, never breaks the app, and fails safe on every malformed input.** All residuals are correctly documented in ADR 0035 or filed as follow-ups (#784/#785). **GO.**</result>

## Part 2 — Test-quality audit (`git diff origin/main...HEAD`)

Reviewed `backend/tests/core/test_rate_limit.py` (pure-unit, 249 lines) and `backend/tests/api/test_rate_limiting.py` (TestClient e2e, 295 lines) against the diff.

### Required failure-mode coverage — all present and correctly asserted

| Scenario | Test | Verdict |
|---|---|---|
| Bearer-rotation from one IP hits the per-IP ceiling (the security fix) | `test_rotating_bearer_hits_ip_ceiling` | ✅ 4 unique tokens pass, 5th 429s, asserts `X-RateLimit-Limit == "4"` (the ceiling, not a token limit) |
| Two distinct tokens share the ipall ceiling | `test_two_distinct_tokens_share_ip_ceiling` | ✅ alternates `token-AAA`/`token-BBB`, 5th (either token) 429s |
| Single token still capped at its own bucket, independent of the ceiling | `test_single_token_still_capped_at_authenticated_limit` | ✅ uses the default `limiter` fixture (AUTH cap=5, IP ceiling=1200 out of the way); asserts `X-RateLimit-Limit == "5"` — proves the token bucket, not the ceiling, fired |
| webhook-with-bearer NOT counted against ipall | `test_webhook_with_bearer_not_counted_against_ip_ceiling` | ✅ 6 bearer-carrying webhook POSTs pass unthrottled (webhook class, cap 50), then confirms a subsequent bearer GET is ipall request #1, not #7 |

| XFF trusted-hops (hops=3 picks correct entry; shorter chain falls back to socket peer, not leftmost) | `test_client_ip_hops_3_picks_client_at_left`, `test_client_ip_hops_3_ignores_spoofed_left_entries`, `test_client_ip_chain_shorter_than_hops_falls_back_to_peer` | ✅ all three, unit-level on `_client_ip` directly |

**No seam-under-test mocking found.** The store injection (`set_store_for_testing`) replaces the documented `RateLimitStore` Protocol, one layer below `rate_limit_middleware` — the middleware itself is always exercised for real via `TestClient` HTTP calls. This is the correct mocking boundary, not a violation.

**No over-broad `except`** in either test file (`grep -n "except"` → zero matches) — nothing here can swallow a failure.

**Webhook class tested against only one provider (`adf`)** — not a concern: `_resolve_policy`'s webhook branch is a bare path-prefix match (`path.startswith("/api/v1/orchestration/events/")`), with zero per-provider branching in the rate-limit code. One representative provider path is sufficient coverage for this seam (unlike the `ORCHESTRATION_PROVIDERS` parametrization concern that applies to actual per-provider orchestration logic).

### 🔴 Hard finding — assertions with side effects (CodeQL `py/side-effect-in-assert`)

`backend/tests/api/test_rate_limiting.py` has **36 instances** of the pattern the audit criteria explicitly call out:

```python
assert ip_ceiling_limiter.get(PROBE, headers=h).status_code != 429   # line 70
assert limiter.post(path, headers=headers).status_code == 429        # line 167
assert c.get(PROBE).status_code != 429                                # lines 265/266/272
# ...33 more, full list at lines 70,79-82,84,93,95,103,125,146-147,151,
# 155-156,165-167,175,182,189-190,201-202,210,243,265-266,272,281-282,284,290-292,294
```

Under `python -O`, every one of these calls (and their side effect — incrementing the rate-limit counter) would be stripped, silently emptying every test in the file of any real exercise. This is exactly the CodeQL `py/side-effect-in-assert` shape (#545). **Fix:** hoist each call, e.g. `resp = ip_ceiling_limiter.get(PROBE, headers=h); assert resp.status_code != 429`.

**Calibration — not counted toward the verdict as a fresh blocker:** the same pattern already exists **57 times** elsewhere in the merged test suite (outside this diff), so this PR is consistent with (not worse than) established practice, and evidently CI's CodeQL job hasn't been gating merges on it to date. I'm flagging it per the audit checklist, but treating it as a systemic pre-existing gap rather than something unique to block PR #783 on. **Recommend `/gh-issue-from-finding`** for a batch cleanup across the whole backend test suite (working agreement #3 — deferred findings must be filed, not dropped).

### Minor observation

- `backend/app/core/rate_limit.py` lines 82–90 (`_get_redis_client`) and 169 (`_now`) are the only uncovered lines in the unit suite — both are thin production-wiring wrappers that unit tests correctly bypass (inject store / monkeypatch clock). I exercised both for real in Part 3 against a live Redis and live wall-clock. Not a gap worth a finding.

No hits found for: mocking the seam under test, orchestration-provider under-parametrization (N/A — no per-provider branching here), untested operational statuses (N/A), covered-but-unasserted branches, missing data-ingesting adversarial coverage (the XFF header parse is lightweight and already covers malformed/empty/whitespace/short-chain inputs — not a persistence/execution ingest path warranting the full `adversarial.py` battery).

<result>## GO / NO-GO: **GO** for the UI dimension

The rate limiter (PR #783 / issue #725, worktree `/Users/arijit/Coding/Python/DataQ/.claude/worktrees/agent-a37794d55abadfaeb`) does not break the frontend, and the one place it visibly interacts with the UI (429s) degrades gracefully. One low-priority parity gap found — recommend a follow-up issue, not a blocker.

### 1. Normal-usage regression — CLEAN on both viewports

Swept Dashboard, Assets, Connections, Suites list + suite detail (all panels: checks, triggers, schedules, notifications, failing-sample columns), a manual "Run Now" + `LiveRunProgress` poll (`GET /runs/{id}/progress`, ~1.5s cadence), Results (Runs tab), run detail, Profile, Admin — at both 1280×800 and 390×844.

- Every `/api/v1/*` call returned 200 across the whole sweep. Zero 429s during ordinary navigation, including during the live-progress poll (only 2 polls fired before the run settled to `failed`, since Snowflake creds aren't live locally — unrelated to this PR).
- Zero horizontal overflow at 390×844 (`scrollWidth === clientWidth` on every page checked).
- One pre-existing console warning, unrelated to this PR: `Warning: [antd: Select] onDropdownVisibleChange is deprecated` on the Suite detail page (both viewports) — not a regression, not filing.
- Confirms the default caps (120/min unauth, 300/min authenticated, 1200/min per-IP ceiling) are generous enough for real dev-proxy usage where all browser traffic collapses to one local IP.

### 2. 429-handling resilience — GRACEFUL (pre-existing generic handling, not new to this PR)

Deliberately fired 150 concurrent `fetch('/api/v1/assets')` from the page context: **116×200 / 34×429**, confirming the unauth 120/min cap fires exactly as configured. Verified the 429 body/headers match ADR 0035: `{"error":{"code":"rate_limited","message":"Too many requests","detail":{"retry_after_seconds":17}}}`, `Retry-After: 17`, `X-RateLimit-Limit: 120`, `X-RateLimit-Remaining: 0`.

Reloaded `/assets` while still throttled, at **both** 1280×800 and 390×844:
- The page renders normally (header, sidebar, layout intact) with an inline antd `Alert`: **"Failed to load assets" / "Too many requests"** — no white-screen, no raw stack, no infinite spinner. Screenshots: `desktop-429-assets.png`, `mobile-429-assets.png` in the scratchpad dir below.
- Side effect worth noting: because the rate limit is a single per-IP bucket shared across *all* unauth endpoints (not per-route), `GET /api/v1/me` was also 429'd on the same reload, and since `is_workspace_admin` has no cached fallback, the **Admin and Settings nav items silently disappeared** from the sidebar while throttled (visible in the mobile/desktop snapshots — the menu had only Dashboard/Assets/Connections/Suites/Results/Profile/Documentation, no Admin/Settings). This is not a crash and self-heals, but it's a slightly confusing symptom (a workspace admin transiently looks like a non-admin) — worth a one-line mention if you write up the PR, not a blocker.
- After the fixed 60s window elapsed, reloading `/assets` again showed full recovery with zero intervention: table data loaded, Admin/Settings nav restored, all `/api/v1/*` calls back to 200.

This is **pre-existing generic error handling** — `frontend/src/pages/Assets.tsx` (and sibling list pages) already catch any failed fetch into a `status: 'error'` state and render an antd `Alert` with `err.message`; `frontend/src/api/client.ts`'s response interceptor already promotes the backend error envelope's `message` field onto `error.message` for any 4xx/5xx. Nothing new had to be built for 429 to degrade safely — it just falls into the same path a 500 or 404 would.

### 3. Parity finding — no dedicated 429 UX (real gap, low priority)

- `frontend/src/components/feedback/ErrorState.tsx:34-38` already has a `429` catalog entry (title "429 — Too many requests", generic subtitle) — but it's wired only to the router 404 catch-all, the `ErrorBoundary` (render-time crashes → 500), and 403 access denials (`Forbidden.tsx`). It is **never invoked for a network 429** from a failed data fetch; list pages use their own inline `Alert`/`message.error(errorMessage(err))` pattern instead (confirmed in `frontend/src/pages/Suites.tsx:216,574`, `frontend/src/hooks/useAsyncAction.ts:17-39`).
- `frontend/src/api/client.ts:30-37`'s interceptor only promotes `error.response.data.error.message` — the string "Too many requests". It never reads `detail.retry_after_seconds` from the body or the `Retry-After` header. Confirmed via `grep -rn "retry_after|Retry-After|retryAfter" frontend/src` → zero hits anywhere in the frontend.
- **Net effect:** a throttled user sees "Too many requests" with no indication of *how long* to wait or that a retry will auto-succeed — they'd have to guess-and-retry. Given the limits are generous (120–1200/min) a normal user is very unlikely to ever see this in practice; this is not a merge blocker for the backend PR.
- **Recommendation:** file a low-priority frontend follow-up, e.g. **"Surface `retry_after_seconds` on 429 responses in the UI (countdown/toast)"** — scope: read `Retry-After`/`detail.retry_after_seconds` in `client.ts`'s interceptor and either wire the existing `ErrorState` 429 catalog entry into a shared toast, or extend `useAsyncAction`/list-page error state to show "Retry in Ns". Since the frontend is otherwise unchanged by #783, this is squarely a `v1.1 Backlog` item, not something that should hold up this PR.

### What's healthy

- Rate limiter is confirmed live in the local stack exactly at the documented limits (verified via `docker exec dataq-api-1 printenv`: `RATE_LIMIT_ENABLED=true`, 120/300/120/1200, XFF hops=1).
- Fixed-window fail-open design (per `backend/app/core/rate_limit.py`) never touched the happy path in this test — no false positives during any normal navigation.
- Self-recovery is real and automatic: no page reload trick, no client-side state to clear, the next request past the 60s window boundary just succeeds.
- Generic error handling already in place across list pages is good enough that a 429 reads no worse than any other transient fetch failure — it just needs the retry-after specificity added on top, which is optional polish.

<note>A task-notification fires each time this agent stops with no live background children of its own. The user can send it another message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than once.</note>
<result>Root cause confirmed with direct evidence. Here's the diagnosis.

## ROOT CAUSE: not fail-open — the limiter is working; the test client's traffic is spread across a /24 of source IPs, so no single per-IP (/32) bucket ever reaches the cap

The rate limiter is **functioning correctly**. The reason the smoke test sees zero 429s is that per-IP bucketing keys on the full /32 client address, and the test traffic egresses from a **rotating NAT/proxy pool** (`2.57.171.0/24`), so each request lands in a *different* bucket, none of which crosses 120.

### Evidence chain (each step eliminates a hypothesis)

1. **Redis reachable + async client + exact prod timeouts all fine.** Ran `redis.asyncio.from_url(REDIS_URL, socket_connect_timeout=0.5, socket_timeout=0.2)` (the merged values) from *inside* the `dataq-app-api` container: `INCR` succeeded in **16.1 ms** (cold), then 4.7/3.6 ms. → Hypotheses 1 (timeouts/TLS), 2 (reachability), 3 (bad URL) **disproven**. `dataq-app-redis` is `Running`; scheme is `redis://` (no TLS), password auth present; both api and worker use the identical `redis-url` secret.

2. **The real prod code path counts correctly — NOT fail-open.** In-container, exercising the actual app modules:
   - `get_settings().rate_limit_enabled = True`, `redis_url` → `dataq-app-redis:6379/0` (matches `os.environ`, password present)
   - `active_store = RedisStore`, `store_override = None`
   - `RedisStore().incr_windows([...]) → [1] → [2] → [3]` — the production store increments fine. → Hypothesis 4 (per-replica store / fail-open) **disproven**.

3. **The smoking gun — keyspace after a reproduction burst.** I fired 200 concurrent unauth requests through the public frontend (`/api/v1/suites`) from this one machine → **all 200 = 401, zero 429** (symptom reproduced). Immediately SCANned `rl:*` in prod Redis:
   ```
   rl:unauth:ip:2.57.171.128:29730096 = 23      rl:unauth:ip:2.57.171.212:... = 26
   rl:unauth:ip:2.57.171.154:...       = 16      rl:unauth:ip:2.57.171.219:... = 19
   rl:unauth:ip:2.57.171.207:...       = 18      ... 11 DISTINCT /32 buckets total
   ```
   200 requests split across **11 distinct source IPs in `2.57.171.0/24`**, each bucket 13–26 — every one far below the 120 cap. The store counted every request; no single IP ever hit the limit. That is exactly why there is no 429, and it is *not* fail-open.

4. **Why the user's `RATE_LIMIT_XFF_TRUSTED_HOPS=1` attempt changed nothing.** The active revision `dataq-app-api--0000044` still has `RATE_LIMIT_XFF_TRUSTED_HOPS=3` in its container spec (and the resolved config reports `xff_hops=3`). The `=1` override never became active on the running replica — ACA env/secret changes are a start-time snapshot and require a new revision/restart (the known "restart ACA after env change" gotcha). So every test — theirs and mine — actually ran at `hops=3`, which correctly resolves the true external client, and that client legitimately spans the /24. (Had `hops=1` truly been live, the rightmost XFF entry is the stable internal-proxy IP, which *would* collapse to one bucket and 429 — but it wasn't live.)

### Async-vs-sync: not the differentiator
Both clients use the same `redis://` + password URL; the async client with the exact prod timeouts works in ~16 ms. Sync Celery on the worker is healthy (Running, exporting telemetry, same secret). The timeouts (0.5 s connect / 0.2 s socket) are generously above the observed ~4–16 ms round-trip.

## Is prod safe right now?
**Yes — no regression, and the app is healthy.** The limiter *is* enforcing per-/32 per minute; a normal single-IP client sending &gt;120/min would get 429s. Redis, the api, and the worker are all Running; unauth requests correctly 401. The only "gap" is a real but pre-existing design property: **per-/32 bucketing is defeated by any client behind a rotating NAT/proxy pool** (CGNAT users, or a distributed low-rate attacker) — and, incidentally, by the smoke-test harness's own egress pool.

Separately confirmed unrelated: App Insights `traces` being empty is a telemetry-ingestion issue (worker exporter POSTs return 200, but the table isn't showing rows) — it did not mask anything here because there is no fail-open occurring.

## Recommended fixes

**To verify enforcement (no code, no config change — test methodology):** drive the burst from a **single stable source IP**, or send an **authenticated** burst with a **fixed** `Bearer` token — that buckets on `rl:default:tok:&lt;sha256&gt;` (cap 300), independent of source IP, so &gt;300 fixed-token requests will 429 regardless of the /24 spread. This will demonstrate the limiter works.

**Do NOT use `hops=1` in prod** as a "fix": besides needing a revision restart to take effect, at `hops=1` the limiter keys on the internal proxy IP and treats *all* external clients as one bucket — self-inflicted global throttle. `hops=3` is correct for the ACA public-envoy→nginx→internal-envoy chain.

**Optional hardening (separate issue + PR, code change):** bucket per-IP on an address *prefix* (e.g. IPv4 /24, IPv6 /64) rather than /32, so NAT/proxy-pool spreading can't trivially dilute the per-IP ceiling. This is a genuine design improvement, not the deployment bug — file it as a follow-up against the rate-limiter (ADR 0035 / #725), don't hotfix.

Net: **config is correct, code is correct, Redis is healthy — nothing to fix on the deployment.** The zero-429 result is a test-methodology artifact of a /24 egress pool, optionally worth a prefix-bucketing enhancement.

Note: I left a couple of tiny throwaway diagnostic keys in prod Redis (`rl_diag_probe`, `rl:diag:appcode:test`, `rl:diag:test`) plus the reproduction's `rl:unauth:ip:2.57.171.*` counters; all are harmless and expire within the 120 s GC window (the two raw ones are single small integers). No code, config, or infra was modified.</result>
